 After investigation, Walmart joins Target in pulling Egyptian cotton sheets Kate Taylor Sep. 9, 2016, 4:54 PM 11,646 facebook linkedin twitter email print AP Walmart is no longer selling Welspun's line of premium Egyptian cotton bed sheets after its supplier was unable to prove the sheets weren't knockoffs. Less than a month after Target announced it would offer refunds for customers who purchased Welspun's Egyptian cotton sheets, Walmart said it is also pulling Egyptian cotton Welspun sheets from its shelves and offering refunds, reports Bloomberg. "Our customers trust us to provide products that are what they say they are on the label," Walmart spokesperson Marilee McInnis said in an e-mail on Friday. "Welspun has not been able to assure us the products are 100 percent Egyptian cotton, which is unacceptable. While the sheets are excellent quality, we are offering our customers a full refund." Any customer seeking a refund can bring their Welspun 100% Egyptian-cotton sheets into a Walmart location to receive a refund. Walmart sold 100% Egyptian cotton bedsheets under the Better Homes & Gardens and Canopy brands. The unsold Egyptian-cotton sheets that are being pull from shelves will be given to Good360, a non-profit that donates companies' excess merchandise to charities.  Target's announcement has set of a series of investigations into Egyptian cotton bed sheets. Target J.C. Penny and Bed Bath & Beyond are also investigating the credibility of their Welspun Egyptian cotton products.  Walmart's news adds credence to the theory that a large percentage of Egyptian cotton sold in the US is fake. While high-quality cotton can be grown around the world, cotton must be grown in Egypt in order to be considered real Egyptian cotton. "When you think about it, 1% of the world's crops are Egyptian cotton. You walk into any store, or look at any one of these websites and see they're all selling Egyptian cotton — it just doesn't add up," Scott Tannen, founder of luxury bedding startup Boll and Branch, told Business Insider in August. "I think [the Target case is] just at the tip of the iceberg." While Tannen has an interest in exposing fake Egyptian cotton, he isn't the only one suspicious of the industry. Earlier this year, the Cotton Egypt Association found that 90% of "Egyptian cotton" sold by retailers tested using a DNA-based authentication program did not contain any cotton produced in Egypt. The association at the time held up Welspun as a symbol of success — something that has clearly since been called into question. Here's how to sell your old one Jennifer Jolly, Special for USA TODAY 4:40 a.m. MST September 9, 2016 Skip Ad Ad Loading... x Embed x Share Ready for Apple's latest and greatest iPhone? Tech columnist Jennifer Jolly has tips on what to do with your old device. This thing is absolutely huge. (Photo: Reviewed.com / Kyle Looney) It happens every September like clockwork. Apple unveils a new smartphone, marking the unofficial start of the fall gadget season, and the official start of people everyone wanting the newest hottest handset. Before you fork over fistfuls of hard earned cash for the next new thing — here’s how to make  bank on what you already have lying around: Sell it to Apple Apple’s new iPhone trade-up program offers store gift cards for iPhone 4’s or newer models. Apple’s flat rates are more static than other trade-in options, which means you won’t likely see them shift much from day to day or week to week. However, the current prices for the iPhone 6 and later are some of the best around, with Apple offering as much as a $250 gift card for an iPhone 6 Plus in great condition. That’s less money than some of the other services, as you’ll read here in a second, but again, many other prices will drop dramatically over the next few days. (The company only accepts iPhones from whatever the previous generations might be though, so I’m out of luck with my 6S until the 7 arrives.) Sell it to a reseller Resellers such as Glyde and Gazelle are great picks again this year too. You go online and answer a few questions about what you have, they estimate how much they’ll pay you for it and send a box for you to mail it in. The last time I checked, Glyde offered $297 for a 64GB iPhone 6 in great condition. The site also warned that it expects prices to drop at least 15% by the time the new iPhone 7 comes out. That’s an issue across the board with many of these services if you don’t have another phone to use between now and getting the new one. USA TODAY What to expect (and what we want) from iPhone 7 Gazelle - Of all the bulk resellers, Gazelle is the most popular, and we’ve talked about it many times here before. Gazelle’s known for great trade-in values and fast payment turnaround times. All you have to do is select the phone, carrier, storage size, and condition from the easy-to-use trade-in tool and then wait for your pre-paid shipping box to arrive. Then, once you have your phone packed up, send it to Gazelle and wait for the cash to roll in. If you don’t want to worry about waiting for your phone to sell elsewhere or making a listing on an auction site, Gazelle is the ultimate no-brainer. If you have an iPhone 6s in decent condition, you can score hundreds of dollars for it. The exact amount will vary depending on the carrier and storage size — for example, a 16GB iPhone 6s on Verizon is worth $242 in excellent condition, but that same phone on T-Mobile is worth $238 — but as long as you’ve kept your phone in good shape, you can expect a solid lump of cash for it. If you have time to do some comparison shopping, double check the prices with Glyde, and others such as Nextworth, which runs a similar trade-in system, and see which one offers the most cash at the moment. uSell - You might not have heard of uSell, but if you’re determined to get the most for your phone you should definitely be considering it as an option. Unlike most other trade-in sites, uSell is actually a hub for many different resellers to attempt to outbid each other for your iPhone. These companies post their best offers on the site, and uSell organizes and matches you with whichever one is promising the best payout. Because of the competitive nature of the site, uSell’s prices can often exceed those on Gazelle and elsewhere, if only by a few bucks. USA TODAY Apple unveils iPhone 7, kills headphone jack Amazon - The world’s largest retailer got into the trade-in game a handful of years ago, and today it’s one of the most popular options. To get started, simply search for the iPhone model you own and see what prices are being offered. Chances are, the value will be similar to what is being offered elsewhere, but because Amazon also takes into account the color of your device, you might discover that your Rose Gold iPhone is worth a tad bit more than the Silver model with the same specs. Once you accept the trade-in offer, you can print a pre-paid shipping label and send the device out at your earliest convenience. The really nice thing about Amazon’s program is that once you lock in your trade-in price you have a full 30 days before Amazon expects it to arrive at their doorstep, which means you can use your phone for those precious couple of weeks until your brand new iPhone shows up. Walmart - If you hadn’t heard, Walmart is all about trade-ins these days, and the iPhone is no exception. You can browse the values for used iPhones on the Walmart site and see exactly how much they’re willing to pay you for your phone. Unlike most other trade-in options, Walmart’s criteria for a trade-in seem much more laid back, with only two quality options — either working or not — and no questions about the color of the device itself. You can trade in either online or in-store, but the one major drawback here is that you are paid in a Walmart gift card, rather than cash, which means you’ll have to buy your new iPhone from Walmart as well. Sell it yourself! If you’re no stranger to the likes of eBay and Craigslist, you might be able to get an even bigger payout than you could at any resale site or store. eBay specifically can be a great place to get lucky with bidders trying to outdo each other, but there’s also a very real risk of a bidder not paying for the phone once they’ve won an auction. That’s a risk for sure, but the reward is a potentially bigger bump in your bank account if it pans out. USA TODAY Incremental Apple should 'swing for the fences' As for Craigslist, there are some who absolutely love it, and if you list an iPhone you’re going to get plenty of attention. As always, try to price your device in line with what the resellers are offering to make sure you don’t get ripped off, and always make your exchange in a public place so you don’t fall victim to some punk trying to run off with your smartphone. Don’t forget to back it up and erase your info No matter how you choose to sell your phone, you should always keep your privacy and security top of mind, and that means wiping your device so that none of your personal info can be salvaged by the buyer. Here’s how to do it: First, sign out of your iCloud account by going into the Settings menu, selecting iCloud, and then tapping Sign Out. If you’re on an older iPhone which is still running iOS 7, you’ll tap Delete Account instead. Once that’s taken care of, go back into your Settings menu and select General, then Reset, and then tap Erase All Content and Settings. Verify your decision and then wait for your phone to wipe itself and reboot. The last step before parting ways with your iPhone is to remove the SIM card, which is located in a small slide-out panel on the side of the device. Find the SIM card slot and open it by inserting the SIM card removal tool into the small hole. If you don’t have a SIM card tool, a paperclip, thread end of a small needle (the more blunt part), or even an earring post (yep, just did it) work well too. Once the slot slides open, just remove the small card inside and close the SIM door again. Now it should be all ready for the next owner to make it their own! When all else fails, recycle responsibly. If your old iPhone isn’t worth the price of someone even paying postage for it, the Apple Renew program is an easy way to dispose of it securely and responsibly. Drop it off at an Apple store or ship it in — they make sure your personal data is destroyed — and then hand it off to Liam. According to Apple, Liam’s a freaky-awesome futuristic “line of robots than can disassemble an iPhone every 11 seconds.” It can also sift, sort, and save more high-quality components than previous methods, recycling more precious materials than ever before. While squirreling away old gadgets might just be a distant cousin to real hoarding — not serious enough yet to have its own reality TV show — there’s no reason to sit on a mountain of old devices. If you have questions, be sure to send us a note or use the comments below. Jennifer Jolly is an Emmy Award-winning consumer tech contributor and host of USA TODAY's digital video show TECH NOW. E-mail her at techcomments@usatoday.com. Subscribe News Sports Business Opinion Entertainment Specialty Lifestyle Jobs Homes Cars Classifieds Weekly Ads 78° Sections Subscription Manage Account Download the new TCPalm app Indian River County Indian River County deputies investigating body found in woods Posted: Sept. 10, 2016 0 Comments SHARE By Nicholas Samuel of TCPalm Posted: Sept. 10, 2016 0 INDIAN RIVER COUNTY — Deputies are investigating a body found Saturday in the woods near Wal-Mart and Applebee's restaurant on State Road 60, said Lt. Eric Flowers, spokesman for the Indian River County Sheriff's Office. A Wal-Mart delivery truck driver pulled in behind the store in the 5500 block of 20th Street when he smelled a terrible smell, Flowers said. The driver walked into the woods on the side of Wal-Mart, found the body and called 911 at 4:30 p.m. The wooded area also is behind the Applebee's restaurant. No signs of foul play are reported and the body is too decomposed to determine a cause of death, Flowers said. The deceased appears to be a homeless man from the clothing found on the body, Flowers said. An autopsy will be performed on the body next week. No more information was available Saturday.   About Nicholas Samuel Nick Samuel is a multimedia journalist for TCPalm.com and Treasure Coast Newspapers who covers breaking news in the afternoons, evenings and weekends across the Treasure Coast. @JournalistNickS nicholas.samuel@tcpalm.com 772-221-4235 0 Share Tweet Email Print News Sections News Home Indian River County Martin County Crime Indian River Lagoon Education State News World News Health News Reader Photos/Videos Obituaries St. Lucie County Photo Galleries Investigations Shaping Our Future Politics National News Strange News YourNews Submit to TCPalm Photo Galleries Fire reported at Islamic Center of Fort Pierce 9/11 remembrance ceremony in Fellsmere Memorial Blue Mass in Jensen Beach September 11th service in Fort Pierce Sandi Paws Pet & People Walk-a-thon Pet Parade in Fort Pierce IRC Intergenerational Recreation Center open house in Vero Beach High School Football: South Fork vs. Palm Beach Lakes High School Football: Fort Pierce Central vs. Clewiston High School Football: Palm Beach Gardens vs. Vero Beach 2nd annual Pack The House at Treasure Coast Food Bank On Sept. 11, 1944, Pietro “Peter” Romano was shot down by the Nazis High School Football: Jensen Beach vs. Fort Pierce Westwood Video Updates Follow us on Twitter Tweets by @TCPalm Now Trending Cleanup of Fort Pierce H.D. News Sports Entertainment Life Opinion Obituaries ePaper Cars Jobs Homes Classifieds log in Site Archive Brooklyn completes Route 6 sidewalks, school roof project Saturday Sep 10, 2016 at 6:50 PM Sep 10, 2016 at 6:50 PM Francesca Kefalas For The Bulletin BROOKLYN — First Selectman Rick Ives can’t help but smile when he’s asked about two projects the town has been trying to complete for years. For the first time in a long time, Ives doesn’t haven’t to explain the latest delay in completing 900-feet of sidewalks to connect Wal-Mart to the rest of the Route 6 commercial district or the issues with putting a new room on the Rose Wing roof at Brooklyn Elementary School. “They’re done,” Ives said. “And they both came in under budget.” Ives is coming to the end of his third year in office. The sidewalks have been on his agenda since he took office, but they discussed before the Wal-Mart was built. Wal-Mart opened in November 2013, the same month Ives was elected. Between the time the store opened and Christmas of that year, three pedestrians were hit in the area. None of the accidents were serious. The sidewalks are on a state road and in early 2014 the Northeast Connecticut Council of Governments won a $300,000 grant for the project. Ives said the bid for the project came in at $98,000. “It’s actually a little embarrassing how off the estimate was,” Ives said. Selectman Joe Voccio said he’s walked to Wal-Mart three times in the two weeks since the sidewalks have been completed. “The nice thing is I saw my first person in a wheelchair using the sidewalk and they didn’t have to be in the road,” Voccio said. “It's doing exactly what we hoped it would do.” “I just saw my first baby carriage being pushed along the sidewalks,” Ives said. “It’s good to see.” Laura Santos said she’s happy the sidewalks are done. She has teenagers at home and it’s nice to know they can walk safely to the store. The Rose Wing roof was completed just before school began Aug. 31. In June 2014 the annual town meeting approved a $65,000 allocation for the project, yet it languished because of changing state regulations. Selectman Bob Kelleher became chairman of the building committee and was able to guide the project through the state regulations. Ives said the final inspection for the roof has not been done, but he expects the final cost of the project at about $35,000. “And we got a little extra work done than we had first intended,” Ives said.  About Us Sign up for daily e-mail Subscribe Site Services Contact Us Customer Service Place an ad Purchase a photo Archives Advertising/Classified Cars Homes Today's Ads Classifieds Obituaries Find Norwich jobs Community Info CtSunlight.org Connecticut tourism The Last Green Valley Sex Offender Registry Gas Buddy DOT traffic cameras Comcast Public Access Television Local Business Northeast Chamber of Commerce Greater Norwich Area Chamber of Commerce Chamber of Commerce of Eastern Connecticut Chamber of Commerce Inc. Sunday marks 15 years since two hijacked planes flew into New York's tallest buildings, bringing them to the ground and killing thousands. A photo of the display shared on Twitter quickly gained thousands of retweets and outraged reactions that the tragic event was being used to sell Coke. A banner above the stack of soft drink boxes, with the Walmart and Coca Cola logos, said: "We will never forget." The display, which has been removed, was designed and created by Coca-Cola, Walmart spokesperson Charles Crowson told local media. "This display was meant to honor local firefighters and to support their organization's upcoming event," Coca-Cola spokeswoman Kimberly Kuo told CNBC. Walmart has been known for its questionable US holiday displays. One store marked Independence Day with a battleship made of Bud Light beer boxes, and for Veteran's Day another store made a soft-drink display in the shape of a bald eagle. Newshub. Mailbag, Sept. 11: Ban political demonstrations; country is sick mailbag@news-press.com 5:02 p.m. EDT September 10, 2016 Foreign policy cartoon by Doug MacGregor (Photo: Doug MacGregor/News-Press) NFL, NBA should ban political demonstration In regard to Colin Kaepernick's refusal to stand for the National Anthem, I think that the NFL and the NBA should ban political demonstration like this. These millionaire athletes should investigate the whole "black lives matter" movement, its a complete fraud, please show me all this prejudice, bias and racism. I never see it. The black community continually complains, but show me, I see the opposite, black racism against whites. Lets get real. Does anyone really believe that police want to kill young black men? - Moe Sinclair, Cape Coral Maybe Warner has lost his moral bearings Concerning Dan Warner’s commentary last weekend on the Kaepernick issue, he stated, “The issue exists only in small minds and the greed of the TV idiots." He then went on a rant of oppressed people and slavery and the downtrodden. He concludes his piece with “Lets forget the debate about what he did and honor him for why he did it." To accuse the majority of Americans to be small-mindedness is hateful and totally disrespectful of our country and all those who made it great and exceptional and those who defended it with their lives and fortunes. If Mr. Warner wants to honor Kaepernick for what he did and “sit with this good man,” he is welcome to do so but he shouldn’t expect hundreds of millions of patriotic Americans to join him. I think Warner’s remarks are spiteful and sarcastic and below a journalist with his credentials. Maybe Mr. Warner has lost his moral bearings and is no linger fit for the job. As for Kaepernick, I and millions of others still think he is a jerk. - Larry Brinegar, Fort Myers Country is sick Just got through reading an article in the News-Press about a Wal-Mart store in Panama City Beach. Seems as though the Wal-Mart manager and the local Coca-Cola bottler thought it would be appropriate to honor local firefighters and support an upcoming event for their organization. A display of Coca-Cola products was arranged to look like the World Trade Center Towers built from Coke Zero products. A backdrop of the American flag was made with red regular Coke, silver Diet Coke and blue Sprite. A banner above the display read “We Will Never Forget." Someone found this display offensive and as a result, Wal-Mart and the Coca-Cola bottler agreed to remove the display. Wal-Mart stated, “the display was not meant to be disrespectful near the anniversary of the September 11 terrorist attack."  Wal-Mart commented further, “We hold this moment in our country’s history in the highest regard, and there was nothing disrespectful intended by the display ... we sincerely apologize that anyone was offended or misunderstood its intent, and we have replaced the display." Pray tell why any red-blooded, patriotic American would be offended at such a display. No American should ever forget this incident. Obviously Wal-Mart doesn’t hold this incident in very high regard after all. Just one more example of people caving to the minority complaints because of perceived political correctness. Who complained, Wal-Mart’s Muslim customers? - Richard West, Cape Coral Safety net Mr. Trump makes us feel good when he assures us that if he is elected we will have the strongest military in the world. He fails to say who will pay for this. It's not likely that he will. We can't count on the many multinational companies who do business in our country and currently pay no taxes. These same corporations provide the money that members of Congress must have to become elected. It affects the way Congress votes. If we had a constitutional amendment that limited donations to $1, Congress would be beholden to "the many."  Our constitution allows a constitutional convention to be convened when 2/3 of the state legislatures ask Congress for it.  Perhaps if the News-Press and other papers support this idea, it would not take long to turn our country around. - Sylvia Richey, Fort Myers Thank you for your service How do you answer when someone says “Thank you for your service?” Here is how I respond: “Thank you. I am proud to have the opportunity to serve.” - Willis K. Smith, North Fort Myers Power of words Words ... Mr. Pitts is still confused about the power of words. Mr. Parker spoke those words. He didn't just misspeak. They are his once spoken. They condemn him the minute they left his mouth. Now you as usual will find some grounds to excuse him. That is not possible for a moral man. You take it further making comparison similar comparing a bird with a stone and hope that once again you can get sly comments in comparing Mr. Parker's comments vs. two others who happen to be white. When will you ever realize all the nonsense you just espoused is divisive. It also pushes those who aren't for Mr. Trump into being for him. Your comparisons could have been directed elsewhere and been more fair and effective. You keep forgetting the "power of words" which lead to phrases which induce thought. Toggle Navigation A-   A+ Sign in News   Stock Home «Back Walmart sourcing non-Egyptian cotton products: Welspun Press Trust of India | Mumbai Sep 10, 2016 09:10 PM IST Home linen major Welspun, which was caught in trouble recently after some of its major US clients stopped sourcing its products, on Saturday said Walmart will continue to source from it barring those products made of Egyptian cotton. Walmart last month followed fellow US retailer Target in recalling Welspun bedsheets and pillow covers after it came to light that the home linen it sold saying as made of Egyptian cotton were not in fact made from the premium yarn typical of the West Asian nation. Walmart used to sell Welspun's sheets and pillow cases under the labels of Better Homes & Gardens and Canopy. In a BSE filing on Saturday, Welspun India, which has appointed consultancy firm E&Y to look into the alleged lapses, said, "Walmart has assured us to do business together. We are working to implement stronger controls and to better label the products we supply to them." The B K Goenka-led company further said, "The product line in question with Walmart accounts for around 1.5 per cent of our business." "We take the current traceability concerns around some of our product lines very seriously, and have been working closely with our retailer partners to support their actions towards a comprehensive resolution programme," Welspun said. The Bentonville, Arkansas-based Walmart on the other hand said in a separate statement that Welspun has not been able to assure us the products are 100 per cent Egyptian cotton, which is unacceptable. "While the sheets are excellent quality, we are offering our customers a full refund," it added. The Amercian retail giant was quick to add that it isn't cutting ties with Welspun. Instead, it is working with Welspun to implement strong controls and better label the products. The Egyptian cotton product portfolio accounts for 6 per cent of Welspun's annual business. The company posted total net sales of Rs 5,387.66 crore in the financial year 2015-16. The problem started after Egypt began to report massive drop in cotton production. According to reports, it produced just 1 per cent of the global cotton last year. The US-based retail chain Bed Bath & Beyond and JC Penny are also conducting third-party audit of items sourced from Welspun, following lapses in supplies by the Gujarat-based firm to Target. Last month, Target Corporation, after extensive investigation, confirmed that Welspun substituted another type of non-Egyptian cotton when producing bedsheets and pillow cases between August 2014 and July 2016. The retailer had said that as soon as its investigation confirmed the substitution, it pulled all remaining product from Target stores and Target.Com and offered the customers full refund. Target said it would end all business with Welspun, one of the world's biggest textile manufacturers, as the vendor was sending it phony Egyptian-cotton sheets. Sales to Target was around $90 million in the FY 2015-16 for Welspun and accounted for almost 10 per cent of its overall business. A Welspun spokesman said on Saturday that the total Egyptian cotton-based sales constituted only about 6 per cent of its $900 million sales. Others among top five of Welspun's customers like Bed Bath and Beyond and JC Penny had said they would also review the matter. Welspun is the biggest exporter of terry towels and bed linen to the US and the company says every fifth towel sold in the US is made by it and two-thirds of its total business comes from the American markets. After Target's recall in mid-August, Welspun's shares tanked by 47 per cent and touched a low of Rs 46.50 on August 30. But since then it has recovered to Rs 59.10 and the share closed at Rs 56.60 on Friday on the BSE. Customers pay a premium for Egyptian cotton products because they are perceived to be softer and more durable. Sheets made from cotton grown in other countries don't always carry the same cachet among Americans. Walmart is one of Welspun's largest customers, while Target, JC Penney, Macy's Inc, Bed Bath and Beyond Inc are also leading customers. According to the US agriculture department, Egypt produced just under 1 per cent of global cotton last year. According to the Egypt Cotton Association, which licences the trademark and certifies suppliers, 90 per cent of products labelled as 'Egyptian cotton' are inauthentic. The $3-billion Welspun Group has interests in textiles, steel, pipes, energy and infrastructure. "Welspun has not been able to assure us the products are 100 per cent Egyptian cotton, which is unacceptable. While the sheets are excellent quality, we are offering our customers a full refund," Walmart Spokesperson said in a statement. It further said: "Walmart is working with Welspun to implement strong controls and better label the products they supply to us." Welspun India, which has appointed consultancy firm Ernst & Young to look into the alleged lapses, however said in a BSE filing: "Welspun and Walmart will continue to do business together. Welspun in working to implement stronger control and better label the products we supply." The company further said: "The product line in question with Walmart accounts for approximately 1.5 per cent of Welspuns business." The Egyptian cotton product portfolio which has come under scanner accounts for 6 per cent of its annual business, it added. The company had posted a total net sales of Rs 5,387.66 crore in the 2015-16. US-based retail chain Bed Bath & Beyond and JCPenny are also conducting third party audit of items sourced from Welspun India, following lapses in supplies by the Gujarat-based firm to the US-based Target. Last month, Target Corporation after an extensive investigation, confirmed that Welspun substituted another type of on-Egyptian cotton when producing Bed sheets and pillows between August 2014 and July 2016. The retailer had said as soon as its investigation confirmed the substitution, it pulled all remaining product from Target stores and Target.com. Sales to Target Corp was approximately USD 90 million in 2015-16 for Welspun India and accounted for almost 10 per cent of its overall business. Vijaywada, Andhra Pradesh:  A huge fire broke out in Walmart's wholesale store near Vijaywada in Andhra Pradesh on Saturday, police said. The fire engulfed a large part of the Best Price modern wholesale store located at Nidamanur, resulting in huge loss of property. There were no casualties in the fire, suspected to have been caused by a short circuit, officials said. "A fire broke at our Best Price store premises in Vijaywada earlier today (Saturday). State Fire authorities quickly reached the store and have brought it under control. We are assessing the damage to the property and investigating the matter. Fortunately, no lives were lost in this unfortunate incident and all our employees and staff are safe," said a spokesperson of Walmart. This is one of the 21 Best Modern wholesale stores owned and operated by Walmart India across the country. Each store offers about 5,000 items in a cash and carry wholesale format. "We have a robust 'Business Continuity Plan' (BCP) to handle all such issues and our BCP team has taken over to quickly restore our store. We are ensuring that our esteemed members don't face any disruption of the services and continues to be served through our nearby Guntur Best Price store," he added.   Trending Movies: Salman Khan, Parineeti, Ram Charan At Sania Mirza's Sister's Sangeet Profit: What Infosys CEO Said On Sending Indian Techies To US After Trump Win Gadgets: Do Not Click or Share That WhatsApp Video Calling Invite Link - It's Fake Related Amazon Courts Food Shoppers Central Vigilance Commission Declines Information On Probe Against Walmart, Mondelez Walmart India Evaluating 'Food-Only' Retail Model In Karnataka, Still Dazzled By The Reddy Show, Tale Of Another Wedding In Karnataka, Still Dazzled By The Reddy Show, Tale Of Another Wedding Share this story on ALSO READWith Notes Ban, Shock And Awe Was Modi's Focus. Last month, US retailer Target Corp severed ties with Welspun after accusing them of passing off cheap sheets as premium Egyptian cotton for two years. "Welspun has not been able to assure us the products are 100 percent Egyptian cotton, which is unacceptable," Wal-Mart said in a statement. The company will pull the products from its stores and website. Wal-Mart said it will not cut ties with Welspun but will work with them to implement strong controls and better label the products. The retailer will offer customers, who purchased the products, a full refund. Egyptian cotton is prized because the length of the cotton fibers are longer, resulting in a finer, lighter more durable fabric and longer-lasting, higher-end clothing. News Sports Entertainment Obituaries Jobs Cars Homes Classifieds E-Edition log in New documents detail Wal-Mart killing of suspected shoplifter Friday Sep 9, 2016 at 8:35 PM Rebecca Baggett told detectives she saw three people running through the parking lot at Wal-Mart just after 3 the morning of Feb. 7. By John Chambliss The Ledger LAKELAND — Rebecca Baggett told detectives she saw three people running through the parking lot at Wal-Mart just after 3 the morning of Feb. 7. "The lady caught up with him, jumped on his back, he fell to the ground and she was punching him in the head, closed fists, um, the gentleman never punched back, he was holding his hands over his head, fell to the ground, got back up, the lady was still punching him, fell back down again, and that's when the third man with the limp came and put his, um, knee in his back," Baggett, a nurse at Lakeland Regional Health, told Lakeland police during an interview. Authorities say that the third man, Randall Eugene Tomko, 58, of Winter Haven, a loss prevention worker, and Crucelis Nunez, 23, a customer service manager at Wal-Mart who lives in Lakeland, killed Kenneth Wisham, of North Lakeland, with help from Nathan Higgins, 35, of Lakeland. Higgins is accused of holding Wisham by the ankles, and pushing his legs up against his buttocks. Higgins' lawyer, Rusty Franklin, has said Higgins played a minor role in the death of Wisham. Charged with manslaughter, the three are out of the Polk County Jail on bail. Nunez, Tomko and Higgins no longer work at Wal-Mart, Erica Jones, a spokeswoman with the company, said in an email. The State Attorney's Office recently released hundreds of pages of documents in the case, which includes interviews from Lakeland Police Department detectives with the defendants, witnesses and the medical examiner's report. According to the investigation, employees chased Wisham outside the U.S. 98 North Wal-Mart and caught him in the grass in the southeast corner of the parking lot before the struggle ensued. Tomko's lawyer, Jeffrey Holmes, said Wisham was committing a strong armed robbery when his client intervened. "He was just doing his job," Holmes said. Holmes said Wisham suffered from numerous ailments that likely contributed to his death. "The bottom line is he was 64, had a heart condition and emphysema," Holmes said. "This guy might have died if he had just fallen down and was held for 30 seconds." Richard McCluskey, a lawyer for Nunez, said he doesn't believe criminal charges should have been filed against his client after the scuffle. He added that Nunez told him that employees called police several times before authorities arrived. 'Let me go, Let me go' The three were charged months after the incident following the release of a medical examiner's report that defined Wisham's cause of death as mechanical asphyxiation. In addition, Wisham suffered 15 broken ribs. District Medical Examiner Dr. Stephen Nelson has said the term ''mechanical asphyxiation'' is used when victims are unable to expand their chests to breathe. In an interview with police, Erica Emerling, an assistant manager at Wal-Mart, said she told her associate to let Wisham go after he was stopped for shoplifting about $400 in DVDs, video games, medicine and a toaster. Wisham grabbed his jacket and began to leave without the cart, while Tomko came out of his office in the store and started to chase Wisham after associates had told him about the shoplifter. During the interview, Emerling told Lakeland Police Detective Stacey Pough she followed Tomko and Nunez outside as they chased Wisham until she reached them and saw the two on top of him with Tomko's elbow on Wisham's back as he pinned him down for about four to five minutes. "He was screaming, 'Let me go, Let me go,' and wiggling," Emerling said. "Then I noticed he went silent." Tomko told police during an interview that Wisham's resistance slowed. "First he was really more physically resistant," Tomko told police. Pough asked how Wisham slowed in his resistance. "He wasn't really saying much," said Tomko, who added he slid off of Wisham as people began to check on him. Emerling asked her employees if Wisham was still breathing. Nunez felt for a pulse, told Emerling she didn't feel anything then Emerling told an associate to call 911. Another employee turned Wisham over and a 911 operator instructs him to perform chest compressions on Wisham until police arrive and continue the chest compressions. An ambulance arrived and emergency technicians rushed to Wisham. Wisham's ribs could have been broken while Tomko was on top of him. Jeremy McCutcheon, a firefighter EMT, told police Wisham never spoke while he attempted to revive the man. McCutcheon said it's common for ribs to break during CPR and chest compressions, but that it appeared Wisham's ribs were already broken. In a separate interview, Andrew Rodriguez, a Polk County Emergency Medical Services firefighter paramedic, agreed that Wisham's ribs were already broken when he attempted CPR. "I know the sensation of breaking ribs and they were already broken when I did 'em for sure, I know that, because it was just very easy to compress," Rodriguez said. The three defendants each face up to 15 years in prison. Higgins is scheduled to be in court for a hearing on Oct. 7. Nunez and Tomko had status hearings in late August. — John Chambliss can be contacted at john.chambliss@theledger.com or 863-802-7588. GoSearch Replay: Eye Opener CW33 TV Schedule Watch CW Shows Search Contact Us CW33 NewsFix Menu NewsFix Eye Opener CW Express Yourself Community Watch CW33 Contact Weather 58° 58° Low 41° High 63° Sat 37° 60° Sun 44° 65° Mon 59° 71° See complete forecast Severe weather alert ‘Study’ Claims Worst Walmart Stores Are In Minority, Poor Neighborhoods Posted 7:08 pm, September 9, 2016, by Shardae Neal Share this: Facebook Twitter Reddit Pinterest LinkedIn Email Please enable Javascript to watch this video NEW YORK, NY -- From coffee to coffins, you can find just about anything in Walmart these days. But if you're shopping around for good customer service a recent study from Columbia University says it'll be hard to spot in Walmarts based in poor or minority communities. The 'study', which looked at about 35,000 Yelp reviews, apparently discovered that the lowest Walmart location ratings came from black or latino neighborhoods. In majority Black zip codes, customers were more likely to use words like "nasty", "unorganized", and "slow" to describe their shopping experience. But, it was opposite with Walmarts in neighborhoods that are the majority white. Reviews there claimed their local Walmart was "friendly" and "clean". In a statement to NewsFix, Walmart says they found the study to be "flawed and without merit." The company also added that they're proud to "provide communities across the country, regardless of social or economic background, access to affordable goods and career opportunities." Whether you take Walmart's word on this or a study based on Yelp reviews - it's kind of hard to just throw this one in the bag! Palomarez Ali V Konneh Angel Latrice Cowen Diamond Prempeh Hector Manuel Guerrero Sr Michael Gray Milton Omar Perez Mousa Toure Samuel S Johnson John Lackey Poleman Hayter Orlando Bradford Judah Jordan David Ryan Howe Andrew Valencia Stephen Romero-Valencia Ronnie Hill Jeremy Lee Nelson Andrew Michael Nelson Mauricio Moraga Robert Villalobos Santiago Sanchez Jamar Roshaun Atkins Melissa Rose Harmsen Francisco Javier Rosas-Molina Luther Cruz Alex Joseph Haider Alan Anthony Dallman Steve Anaya Clifford Frederick Gant Enrique Guzman-Castro Slideshow: PHOTOS: KOLD News 13 September Mugshots Police records detail late night standoff in Tucson 2016-09-09T23:25:29Z2016-09-09T23:55:33Z By Craig Reck, Reporter Email Connect creck@tucsonnewsnow.com Jeremy Lee Nelson (Source: Tucson Police Department) TUCSON, AZ (Tucson News Now) - A man at the center of a police standoff in Tucson talked about a shoot out with police hours before being taken into custody in a shopping center parking lot, according to police records. Jeremy Lee Nelson asked an acquaintance for a ride to the airport and mentioned a shootout with police while she drove. She told police Nelson wanted to stop at a Walmart first, where he dropped a handgun in a trash can then picked it back up and returned to her white van. The arrest report shows Nelson's acquaintance was afraid and contacted police. She told them about his gun and propane tank when an officer arrived on scene. More officers responded to the area of Drexel and Tucson Boulevard to asses the situation. Hostage negotiators and the mental health unit were called in, according to police records. Nelson told officers they were trying to kill him and that he only wanted to speak with U.S. Marshals or deputies from the Pima County Sheriff's Department. Tucson Fire Department was called in because several officers worried about the smell of propane, but the air quality was okay, according to TPD documents. A couple officers noted in their reports that Nelson appeared to be using methamphetamine or crack. He fell asleep at one point and officers managed to break a window in the van, according to the report. Nelson asked for water and cigarettes at one point, but would not leave the van to retrieve them. The reports state he did the same thing for dog food and water, but again, wouldn't leave. TPD tried using pepper bells around the van, but Nelson did not move, according to police records. The report states that when Nelson started talking about what should happen to his dog and referencing his own death, officers decided to take action. They breached the van door, restrained Nelson, used a taser and arrested him before he could fire his gun. It was loaded with a round in the chamber, according to police records. The standoff lasted approximately six hours. Nelson is in the Pima County Jail on a $25,000 cash bond. Court records show that Nelson is charged with possession of dangerous weapon by a felon. TPD added the following statement to Nelson's interim complaint: "Second incident involving criminal misconduct and threats to the public in a 48 hour period. The defendant has demonstrated and displayed several homicidal and suicidal ideations in addition to acquiring firearms." According to Pima Count Superior Court, Nelson was convicted in 2002 for burglary and drug charges. Copyright 2016 Tucson News Now. All rights reserved. FRIDAY, NOVEMBER 18, 2016 Toggle navigation Main menu News Local news National news World news Community news Education Police logs Calendar New England Lotteries Daniel Pearl Scholarship Sports Local sports Red Sox Yankees Patriots Giants Celtics Bruins Business Business news Real estate news Entertainment The 413 Berkshires Week Berkshires Week calendar Theater reviews Movie reviews The Ultimate Dining Guide Horoscopes TV listings Lifestyles Insights Berkshire lifestyles Health Food & recipes Outdoors Best of the Berkshires Announcements Opinion Editorials Letters to the editor Columnists Blogs Obituaries Today's obituaries View all Publications Special sections Book of Homes Berkshire Business News Marketplace Jobs Classifieds Top listings Place an ad Legal Notices Weekly Flyers Tools e-Edition Contact us Subscriber services Newspapers in Education RSS Letter: Numbers add up against Walmart supercenter plan Posted Friday, September 9, 2016 4:28 pm The Berkshire Eagle Numbers add up against Walmart supercenter plan To the editor: The article in the Sunday, Sept. 4, Eagle titled "Labor Council opposes Walmart," with information on Waterstone Retail Development's proposed Walmart supercenter at the Stanley Business Park, prompted me to do some elementary school arithmetic with the figures cited in the article. First I looked at the map of the site which you can also do at woodlawncrossing.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/site-map.jpg. You will see the proposed supercenter sketched on site 9. This site is described as a 15-acre site at the URL williamstanleybp.com/site-9/. The article states that the entire business park is 52 acres, so the supercenter will occupy just under 29 percent of the total acreage! Is this the development magnet, the innovation center, that the Berkshires needs to retain its residents and attract new ones? Let's do more arithmetic. If we take an acre to equal 40,000 square feet, we calculate site 9 to be 600,000 square feet. The supercenter size as stated in the article will be 190,000 square feet, so if we divide 190,000 by 600,000 we learn that almost 32 percent of site 9 will be Walmart retail space. The remaining 68 percent will be parking spaces! Look closely at the site map and you'll see them sketched in. So the much-touted business park will devote more than two-thirds of the "teens parcel" to asphalt, if this is the best Pittsfield can do. Along with the poor-paying jobs, attack on local small businesses, shoddy foreign-made goods, we will be the "beneficiaries" of about 10 more acres of asphalt. For all our sakes, I hope Pittsfield can do much better. Mary Jane Incorvia Mattina, Lenox Print Email Tweet TALK TO US If you'd like to leave a comment (or a tip or a question) about this story with the editors, please email us. We also welcome letters to the editor for publication; you can do that by filling out our letters form and submitting it to the newsroom.  After investigation, Walmart joins Target in pulling Egyptian cotton sheets Kate Taylor Sep. 9, 2016, 4:54 PM 11,646 facebook linkedin twitter email print AP Walmart is no longer selling Welspun's line of premium Egyptian cotton bed sheets after its supplier was unable to prove the sheets weren't knockoffs. Less than a month after Target announced it would offer refunds for customers who purchased Welspun's Egyptian cotton sheets, Walmart said it is also pulling Egyptian cotton Welspun sheets from its shelves and offering refunds, reports Bloomberg. "Our customers trust us to provide products that are what they say they are on the label," Walmart spokesperson Marilee McInnis said in an e-mail on Friday. "Welspun has not been able to assure us the products are 100 percent Egyptian cotton, which is unacceptable. While the sheets are excellent quality, we are offering our customers a full refund." Any customer seeking a refund can bring their Welspun 100% Egyptian-cotton sheets into a Walmart location to receive a refund. Walmart sold 100% Egyptian cotton bedsheets under the Better Homes & Gardens and Canopy brands. The unsold Egyptian-cotton sheets that are being pull from shelves will be given to Good360, a non-profit that donates companies' excess merchandise to charities.  Target's announcement has set of a series of investigations into Egyptian cotton bed sheets. Target J.C. Penny and Bed Bath & Beyond are also investigating the credibility of their Welspun Egyptian cotton products.  Walmart's news adds credence to the theory that a large percentage of Egyptian cotton sold in the US is fake. While high-quality cotton can be grown around the world, cotton must be grown in Egypt in order to be considered real Egyptian cotton. "When you think about it, 1% of the world's crops are Egyptian cotton. You walk into any store, or look at any one of these websites and see they're all selling Egyptian cotton — it just doesn't add up," Scott Tannen, founder of luxury bedding startup Boll and Branch, told Business Insider in August. "I think [the Target case is] just at the tip of the iceberg." While Tannen has an interest in exposing fake Egyptian cotton, he isn't the only one suspicious of the industry. Earlier this year, the Cotton Egypt Association found that 90% of "Egyptian cotton" sold by retailers tested using a DNA-based authentication program did not contain any cotton produced in Egypt. The association at the time held up Welspun as a symbol of success — something that has clearly since been called into question. Epoch Times on Facebook US News Wal-Mart: Coke Display Stacked Like Twin Towers Removed US News Wal-Mart: Coke Display Stacked Like Twin Towers Removed By Associated Press | September 9, 2016 AT 4:41 PM Last Updated: September 9, 2016 4:41 pm (AP Photo/Jae C. Hong, File) NEW YORK—Wal-Mart says a display of Coke cans stacked to look like the World Trade Center has been removed from a Florida store, and was not meant to be disrespectful near the anniversary of the Sept. 11 terrorist attack. The display was mocked online after a photo was posted on Twitter, and Buzzfeed wrote about it. The photo showed the World Trade Center towers built of Coke Zero packages. A backdrop of the American flag was made with red regular Coke, silver Diet Coke and blue Sprite. A banner above the display said, “We will never forget,” with the Coca-Cola and Wal-Mart logos in a corner. Walmart said in a statement the display was removed Wednesday. Today, we are no longer a Post 9/11 society. Today, we are a Post Wal-Mart Depicting 9/11 With Coke Cans Society. pic.twitter.com/kwCQntWebU — Gabriel Gundacker (@gabegundacker) September 8, 2016 “We hold this moment in our country’s history in the highest regard, and there was nothing disrespectful intended by the display,” it said. The company said the design for the display for the store in Panama City Beach, Florida, came from the supplier, and was approved by its store management. The Coca-Cola bottler for the region said the display was meant to honor local firefighters and support an upcoming event for their organization. “We sincerely apologize that anyone was offended or misunderstood its intent, and we have replaced the display,” the bottler said. About Us   Log in or Register!   Top News U.S. News World News Entertainment Movies Music TV Odd News The Almanac Business Security Industry Energy Industry Sports Fantasy Football NFL NBA MLB NHL Golf Tennis College Football College Basketball Science Health Opinion Photos Latest Photos 2016 Olympics News Entertainment Sports Features Archives Archive Home / Odd News Walmart, Coke apologize for Sept. 11-themed display at Florida store By Ben Hooper   |   Sept. 9, 2016 at 3:43 PM Follow @oddnewsupi Comments Florida c'mon man pic.twitter.com/HU4y2rxgFG— Shawn (@online_shawn) September 6, 2016 PANAMA CITY, Fla., Sept. 9 (UPI) -- A Walmart spokesman said a 9/11-themed display at a Florida store was designed and created by Coca-Cola. A photo of the display at the Walmart in Panama City, Fla., was posted to Twitter by user @online_shawn and immediately sparked outrage among online commentators who objected to the use of the Sept. 11, 2001, attacks to sell Coke, as well as the arrangement of the Coke boxes to resemble the twin towers in front of an American flag. "We will never forget," reads a banner bearing the Coca-Cola and Walmart logos. Walmart spokesman Charles Crowson said the display was being removed following the online outcry. Crowson told the Orlando Weekly the display was pitched to Walmart by Coke, and the store approved it. "We hold this moment in our country's history in the highest regard, and there was nothing disrespectful intended by the display being assembled. It was removed from our Florida store Wednesday," Walmart said in a statement emailed to Mashable. Coca-Cola spokeswoman Kimberly Kuo said the display was misinterpreted. "This display was meant to honor local firefighters and to support their organization's upcoming event," she told CNBC. "We sincerely apologize that anyone was offended or misunderstood its intent, and we have replaced the display." TidewaterBiz Peninsula stores fight for grocery dollars Hampton Roads grocery store market share rankings TidewaterBiz.com reports grocery rankings in our local area. TidewaterBiz.com reports grocery rankings in our local area. Tara BozickContact Reportertbozick@dailypress.com Who are the top grocers in Hampton Roads? Privacy Policy Peninsula grocers are adapting to give customers what they expect — healthy, quality food at affordable prices — as Wal-Mart, Kroger and Whole Foods continue to grab more market share in the region. Of the total Hampton Roads market share, Food Lion remains the dominant grocer with Wal-Mart at No. 2 and Farm Fresh at No. 3, according to trade publication Food World's annual market study report. On a more local level, Food Lion is the favorite for Newport News, Hampton, Isle of Wight, Smithfield and Mathews while shoppers in James City and Williamsburg prefer Farm Fresh, according to the report. Wal-Mart dominates in Gloucester while the big-box retailer barely beats out Food Lion in York County. Food Lion remains the dominant grocer in Hampton Roads, according to trade publication Food World's annual market study report. Check out the full list. Regionwide, Food Lion dominates because it has the most stores with 78 to garner 17.8 percent of total market share, according to the report. Farm Fresh took a dip from 13.9 percent to 12.9 percent of total market share from 2015 to 2016. Wal-Mart, including its smaller Neighborhood Markets, had a slight increase in total market share from 14.8 percent to 14.9 percent from year to year. Other alternative grocers, including 7-Eleven, Wawa, Walgreens and Sam's Club, also gained ground with alternatives now representing 51.6 percent of the market, up from 51.2 percent in 2015. Military commissaries, which represent 10 percent of the Newport News and Hampton market share, saw a total regional market share dip from 4.9 percent in 2015 to 4.4 percent this year, according to the Food World report. Kroger's addition of Marketplace stores in Hampton Roads contributed to its increase in total market share from 4.76 percent to 4.84 percent, according to the Food World report. Caption Video: Hampton's "State of the City" Mayor Donnie Tuck gave the "State of the City" address at the Hampton Roads Convention Center on Tuesday, Nov. 15, 2016. Mayor Donnie Tuck gave the "State of the City" address at the Hampton Roads Convention Center on Tuesday, Nov. 15, 2016. Caption Why electric cars will be the way of the future Electric cars account for less than 1% of U.S. new car sales right now, but that number will most likely increase in the future. Electric cars account for less than 1% of U.S. new car sales right now, but that number will most likely increase in the future. Hampton Roads is already a highly competitive market where price remains the primary driver with strong low-price influence from Wal-Mart and the commissaries, according to the report. And it's only going to get more competitive as discount retailers Aldi and Lidl plan to enter the market and as Kroger plans more stores on the Peninsula — in Denbigh and in the redevelopment of Riverdale Plaza in Hampton. Keep your eye on Food Lion's sustainability in Hampton Roads when German discount grocer Lidl starts entering the market in 2018 with nine stores planned so far in the region, including two in Newport News and one in Hampton, Food World Publisher Jeff Metzger said. The millennial generation, or the 18-34 age group, is driving a lot of change toward nutrition and wellness as well as convenience, Metzger said. That's why you see grocers adapting with better marketed organic and natural food sections and a better selection of prepared food or ready-to-cook items. Over the years, Hampton Roads' changing demographics has led to households with more disposable income, demanding higher end stores and selection, Metzger said. Whole Foods is the case in point in Newport News, where Mid-Atlantic favorite Wegmans also had its eye. Grocers are also adding improved private-label products, which could appeal to those who aren't as brand loyal, Metzger said. What grocery store chain is the Peninsula still missing? Do you want to see a Wegman's? A Publix? Here's a partial look at missing supermarkets. For instance, Food Lion recently took its premium-tier Taste of Inspirations deli line companywide, said Wanda Marshburn, Food Lion director of operations for 25 stores in the Newport News-Hampton region. Salisbury, N.C.-based Food Lion, which is part of the Ahold Delhaize group, continues to invest to keep low prices on staple items and has been enhancing stores to showcase its fresh produce and natural and organic items, Marshburn said. Food Lion makes buying natural or premium products more affordable with its own brands, including its own wine, she added. Food Lion also remains strong because of its convenient neighborhood locations and dedicated employees, Marshburn said. Farm Fresh has been remodeling stores on the Peninsula to modernize the shopping experience, said Dave Huettl, vice president of sales and merchandising. From 2014 to the end of 2016, Farm Fresh will have remodeled 18 of its 41 stores in Hampton Roads, including seven of 12 Peninsula stores. Much of those renovations have focused on highlighting its fresh products in addition to revamping the deli, bakery and seafood departments, Huettl said. (Judith Lowery) Throughout the store, Farm Fresh is allocating more space to capture customer trends for healthier options, including organic and gluten-free items, and its chef-to-go items to make it easier for folks who want to cook gourmet-style meals at home, Huettl said. The company is also adding more items to the Wild Harvest line. "We try to give you a convenient meal solution regardless of the size of your family," Huettl said. Farm Fresh finds more folks want healthier meal options and transparency in labeling, he said. Still, Virginia Beach-based Farm Fresh, a subsidiary of Minnesota's SuperValu, might appeal to millennials who are focused on the local community. "Being in the area, we're always trying to highlight who's local, what's local in our weekly ads in the store," Huettl said. While Cincinnati-based The Kroger Co. and its Village Square at Kiln Creek shopping center store compete well on price, the biggest change the company has seen during the past five years has been the customer emphasis on convenience, spokeswoman Noelle Motley said in an email. That's why the company is rolling out its ClickList online ordering service at stores in South Hampton Roads this year. Kroger now operates 10 stores in the region, including four Marketplace stores that sell home decor, bed and bath items and small appliances. The new Marketplaces and providing items customers ask for, such as natural and organic foods, local produce and craft products, have helped Kroger's regional uptick in sales, Motley said. Millennials also like the digital coupon savings and prepared foods. Harris Teeter has been able benefit from its January 2014 merger with The Kroger Co. to pass savings on to shoppers with lower prices on thousands of products, said spokeswoman Lea Ramsey. Harris Teeter's market share in Hampton Roads grew from 6.08 percent to 6.15 percent, according to Food World. The grocer also prides itself on its quality products, extensive selection, clean stores, friendly staff and promotions. The Fresh Market, which saw its regional market share increase from 1.06 percent to 1.29 percent, had already been providing shoppers easy grab-and-go options for preparing a home-cooked meal, said spokeswoman Stephanie Lowder. The "Little Big Meal" program changes meals each week. Food World's market analysis is based on information collected from April 1, 2015, through March 31, 2016. Find the full report at best-met.com/issue/market-study-2016/. Bozick can be reached by phone at 757-247-4741. Sign up for a free weekday business news email at TidewaterBiz.com. If you'd like to learn more... - A A + Listen A soda display at a Florida Walmart fashioned to commemorate 9/11 and look like the Twin Towers has drawn divisive responses from social media and local residents. Story continues below Set up under a banner that read “We Will Never Forget,” emblazoned with both the Walmart and Coca-Cola logos, stacks of soda cases were used to create an American flag and Twin Towers mosaic. One shopper at the Panama City Beach location told WJHG that she found it offensive. I don’t think that’s right,” she said. Others saw it as an important reminder of the tragic events 15 years ago. “It’s something that was terrible that happened to us in our country. We should not hide it or be offended by it,” said one woman. “Anything that’s patriotic is fine. No matter whether it’s selling something or doesn’t. It’s telling people, to remind people to think of America, America first,” said a man. Subscribe News Sports Business Opinion Entertainment Specialty Lifestyle Jobs Homes Cars Classifieds Weekly Ads 78° Sections Subscription Manage Account Download the new TCPalm app Bargainista Small grocery stores mean big savings on the Treasure Coast The grand opening for the new Aldi at 3937 S.E. U.S. 1 is Sept. 15. The first 100 shoppers will receive store gift certificates, free reusable bags, samples and entry in a contest to win free produce for a year. (KELLY TYKO/TREASURE COAST NEWSPAPERS) Posted: Sept. 09, 2016 1 Comment SHARE Aldi opens its third Treasure Coast store Sept. 15 in Stuart at the southeast corner of U.S. 1 and Southeast Miami Avenue near the Walmart Supercenter. (KELLY TYKO/TREASURE COAST NEWSPAPERS) Related Coverage BARGAINISTA: Tips for shopping at Aldi Posted: Sept. 09, 2016 1 Just because a store is small, doesn't mean you can't save big. I've found this to be the case at the Treasure Coast's new wave of smaller grocery stores, especially no-frills discount grocery retailer Aldi. The German grocer opens its third store here Thursday in Stuart at the southeast corner of U.S. 1 and Southeast Miami Avenue near the Wal-Mart Supercenter. Another Aldi is expected to open this winter in Port St. Lucie. Not to be outdone, Wal-Mart is continuing to bring its smaller grocery-only stores to the region. Wal-Mart Neighborhood Market stores are scheduled to open early next year in Vero Beach and Port St. Lucie. The smaller stores — a typical Aldi is 18,539 square feet and a Neighborhood Market is one-fifth the size of a Supercenter — make shopping trips faster. NEW ALDI Aldi, one of the world's largest grocery chains, is short for "Albrecht Discount," named after brothers and original owners Karl and Theo Albrecht. A California offshoot of Aldi operates the trendier Trader Joe's, a gourmet and specialty grocer whose closest stores are in Palm Beach Gardens and Wellington. The grand opening for the new Aldi, at 3937 S.E. U.S. 1, begins with a ribbon cutting at 8:45 a.m. After the ceremony, the first 100 shoppers will receive store gift certificates, free reusable bags, samples and entry in a contest to win free produce for a year. "We are pleased to bring our first store to Stuart to help customers get high-quality products at everyday low prices," said Chris Hewitt, Aldi's Royal Palm Beach division vice president, in a news release. "We challenge shoppers to switch from national brands to our high-quality exclusive brands and stretch their dollars without compromising quality." Like with past Aldi grand openings, I expect many dedicated shoppers will line up early or possibly camp out. However, a competing grand opening — the region's first Wawa also opens Thursday in Stuart at the southeast corner of Kanner Highway and Monterey Road — might split the crowds. Aldi stores primarily carry items most commonly purchased at grocery stores and don't have pharmacy, bakery and deli departments. The store brands are more than 1,300 products and the company says it keeps prices low by using a warehouse layout and minimal staffing. Another cost-saving measure is customers "rent" shopping carts for a quarter. As long as you return your cart, you'll get the quarter back. You also need to bring your own bags and then bag your own groceries. Since Aldi started accepting credit cards in March, I've been a regular shopper and my favorite things to purchase are produce and eggs because of how low the prices are. Because of the store's generous "Double Guarantee," I'm willing to be adventurous and try other products. With the guarantee, if you're not 100 percent satisfied with a product, bring it back and Aldi will replace the product and refund your money. FUTURE STORES Two Wal-Mart Neighborhood Market stores are under construction and more could be in the works. Like the region's first market in St. Lucie West, the old Vero Beach Albertsons, which closed in June 2012, is being replaced by a grocery-only Wal-Mart. A second Port St. Lucie store is being built at the northwest corner of Port St. Lucie Boulevard and Yale Street, north of Darwin Boulevard. A Wal-Mart Neighborhood Market also could replace the Fort Pierce Winn-Dixie that closed in 2013 on U.S. 1 in the Kmart plaza, according to plans on real estate website LoopNet. Wal-Mart officials would not comment on this but if it happens perhaps Aldi would open a store nearby too. Not far from where the Port St. Lucie Wal-Mart is under construction, the city's second Aldi is being built at Gatlin Boulevard and Brighton Street and expected to open this winter, Hewitt said in an email statement. But what about an Aldi in Indian River County? While preliminary plans were filed for a location on State Road 60 near the Wal-Mart Supercenter earlier this year, formal plans haven't been filed yet with the county. The proposed store could go in a plaza on a 9.5-acre lot between the Applebee's and Sonny's BBQ being proposed by Konover South, the same developer of the Stuart Aldi. Although Hewitt said he had no details he could share about a possible Indian River or Vero Beach location, I firmly believe the company will eventually open a store in the county. If not on State Road 60, maybe near the new Wal-Mart. And since Aldi and Wal-Mart are continuing to add stores throughout Florida, I think we'll have more places to shop in the future. Kelly Tyko is a columnist for Treasure Coast Newspapers. This column reflects her opinion. AccuWeather.com Quick Look Change your current location » View Full Weather Report Search Search Search syracuse.com Account Sign In Close Sign in to syracuse.com You are signed in as Edit Public Profile Sign Out Classifieds Classifieds Home Autos Obituaries Jobs Real Estate Rentals Garage Sales Coca-Cola apologizes for 9/11 display resembling twin towers at Walmart By  Geoff Herbert | gherbert@syracuse.com The Post-Standard Email the author Follow on Twitter on September 09, 2016 at 8:35 AM, updated September 09, 2016 at 9:28 AM Print Email Twitter  Coke Zero meets Ground Zero? Coca-Cola has apologized for a 9/11 display that resembled the World Trade Center before the 15th anniversary of the Sept. 11, 2001, terrorist attacks. Photos online went viral showing cases of Coke cans stacked to look like the twin towers in a Walmart store in Florida. Black Coke Zero cases were in columns, surrounded by red Coca-Cola, gray/white Diet Coke and blue Sprite cases in the shape of the American flag. Above the display was a sign with Coca-Cola and Walmart's logos and the message: "9-11-01: We will never forget." Under the banner is a "Rollback" sign advertising that 12-packs of the soda cans were on sale for $3.33 each. Wal-Mart said store management at its Panama City Beach, Fla., location approved the design, which was criticized as "exploitive" and "disgusting" on social media this week. Two jobs open today. One at @CocaCola for this display idea to honor 9-11. And the mgr at @Walmart that approved it pic.twitter.com/dtGKcLr2Zh— Bert Weiss (@BertShowBert) September 8, 2016 After backlash, Wal-Mart said the display was removed from the store on Wednesday. "We hold this moment in our country's history in the highest regard, and there was nothing disrespectful intended by the display," the retailer told the Associated Press. Coca-Cola's bottler for the region told the AP it was meant to honor local firefighters for an upcoming event "We sincerely apologize that anyone was offended or misunderstood its intent, and we have replaced the display," the bottler said. This isn't the first time a brand has been accused of using events like 9/11, where nearly 3,000 people were killed in terrorist attacks coordinated by Osama bin Laden and al-Qaeda, to promote products. In 2013, AT&T came under fire for "tacky" ads showing a smartphone taking a photo of the twin lights paying tribute to the former WTC towers in New York City, and Marriott customers found the hotels' offer of free coffee and muffins "in remembrance" to be offensive. Search Contact Us Sign In | Sign Up Home Shows All Staff Schedule Bernadette Lee Rob Kirkpatrick Brandon Comeaux Ken Romero Dr. John Sutherlin Listen Listen Live Mobile Events Full Calendar Submit an Event News Junkies Sign Up Contests VIP Support Win Stuff Contact Us Help & Contact Info Send Feedback Advertise Experts Acadian Total Security Audio Video Innovators Barczyk Chiropractic Group Brown’s Furniture Showplace Coccolare Spa Eagle Pest Control and Chemical GMFS Mr Electric National Foundation Repair Piggly Wiggly Theriot Family Dental Care Follow on Facebook Follow on Twitter Subscribe on YouTube Follow on Instagram Tip Us Noteworthy: Win KPEL Cash Banquet Pick Em 2016 Wingin’ It Wednesday Legal Authority Lafayette Live Gas Prices Crime Florida Walmart Faces Backlash Over Controversial 9/11-Themed Coca-Cola Display [PHOTO] By DJ Digital September 9, 2016 6:35 AM Share on Facebook Share on Twitter Coca-Cola and Walmart are facing sharp criticism over a 9/11-themed store display of the Twin Towers in front of the American flag. The in-store display—made entirely from cans—was accompanied by a sign saying “We will never forget” flanked by logos for both Coca-Cola and Walmart. The sign and the display were created to mark the 15 year anniversary of the 2001 attack that took the lives of nearly 3,000 people. Almost immediately after being posted on the internet, the photo (taken at a Panama City Beach Walmart) received backlash from those who thought the display was in poor taste. Florida c'mon man pic.twitter.com/HU4y2rxgFG — Shawn (@online_shawn) September 6, 2016 According to the Orlando Weekly, employees at the Panama City Beach Walmart say they were only following orders and that the 9/11 display was “all Coke’s idea.” This is definitely not the first time Walmart has come under fire for questionable store displays (does anyone remember that time they built a tank out of Bud Light to commemorate the 4th of July?) but the display has been dismantled at the time of this post. Many argue that while the intentions may be genuine, it is in poor taste to market a product and/or profit off the 9/11 anniversary. Others feel that those who are offended are simply being too sensitive. What do you think? A grand opening will be held Oct. 1. By Dennis Seid Daily Journal Some former Walmart Express locations are reopening this weekend as Dollar General stores. Dollar General bought 41 of the former Walmart Express stores in 11 states for an undisclosed sum in July. Included in the purchase were five locations in Mississippi: Belmont, Derma, Mantachie, Nettleton andSardis. Dollar General did not buy the location in Walnut, but it does have a store there. The new expanded Dollar General stores – which offer fresh meat, produce and fuel – are having soft openings in Belmont, Mantachie and Nettleton on Saturday. Dollar General said it will celebrate the stores’ official grand openings later this month and next month. At each grand-opening event, which will begin at 8 a.m., the first 50 adult customers will receive a free three-pound package of ground beef, the first 100 adult customers will receive a $10 Dollar General gift card and the first 200 shoppers will receive a Dollar General tote bag with assorted samples, among other giveaways. Donuts and coffee will be served in the morning while hot dogs and drinks will be available beginning at 11 a.m. Belmont and Mantachie will have grand openings on Sept. 24, while the Nettleton store will have its event Oct. 1 The store in Derma still is being renovated and will open in “mid-fall,” according to Dollar General. The new stores are about12,000 square feet, compared to a traditional Dollar General format that is some 9,100 square feet. Each of the new stores will employ about 15 people. “Dollar General is committed to delivering a pleasant shopping experience that includes a convenient location, a wide assortment of merchandise and great prices on quality products,” said Dan Nieser, Dollar General’s senior vice president of real estate and store development. “We hope our customers will enjoy shopping at Dollar General’s new locations.” dennis.seid@journalinc.com Twiter: @dennisseid Click here to leave a comment!
