National World Business Tech Sport Entertainment Life & Style Travel Motoring Profile Settings Sign Out business Search Industries Small Business Money Farming World Better Business Nurture Change 2016 Opinion & Analysis Tools The practice of using 9/11 to market consumer goods backfires TRAVIS M ANDREWS Last updated 13:47, September 9 2016 @online_shawn/TWITTER Companies across the United States employ remarkably tone-deaf marketing strategies that somehow reference 9/11. As the 15th anniversary of 9/11 approaches, many Americans are preparing themselves for a day of reflection. For some, it will involve mourning. For others, it will be an opportunity to look forward. But for some folks who work in marketing, it'll be another chance to do a little #branding. Each year, companies across the US employ remarkably tone-deaf marketing strategies that somehow reference 9/11. This year is no different, as evidenced by a Coca-Cola display prominently erected in the middle of a Walmart in Panama City Beach, Florida. READ MORE: * Change, crash, burn: Seven top re-branding failures * Maori TV wrestles with brand identity as it seeks more viewers * BP loses fight for the colour green * Products that flopped worse than Coke Life The display is composed of 12 packs of Coca-Cola original (red boxes), Diet Coke (silver boxes) and Sprite (blue boxes) arranged in the shape of a giant American flag. Before the flag stands two large rectangles composed of 12 packs of Coke Zero (black boxes), which are clearly meant to represent the twin towers. Hanging above the display is a banner bearing both Coca-Cola and Walmart's logos. Over an image of the pre-9/11 New York City skyline are the words "We Will Never Forget," and in the top right corner is "9-11-01." Under the banner is a sign announcing that Coca-Cola 12 packs are on sale for $3.33. "Rollback," the sign states. The display first came to the public's attention through a tweet by a user named @online_shawn, which has been retweeted 2,955 times and liked 4560 times. Florida c'mon man pic.twitter.com/HU4y2rxgFG— Shawn (@online_shawn) September 6, 2016 Ad Feedback Needless to say, anger rolled in. "This is one of the lamest things I've ever seen," tweeted one user. Another called it "crass commercialization." "Utterly tasteless," tweeted a third. "Is that real?!" asked one user. "Dear God, tell me that isn't real." Etcetera, ad nauseam. Walmart spokesman Charles Crowson told the Orlando Weekly that the display, which was conceived by Coke and approved by Walmart, was currently being taken down. Neither Walmart nor Coke is the first company to come under fire for invoking the national tragedy as a means to sell stuff. Each year, companies roll out deals and tweets associated with the attacks, and each year they face a tidal wave of backlash and outrage in response. One of the more galling examples came in 2014 when the Birmingham, Alabama-based clothing company Tied to the South requested 2,296 retweets, one for each person who had lost his/her life in the attack. The tweet showed one of the towers, just after the attack. The tweet, like all of the following examples, has been removed after public outcry but not before an intrepid Internet user snapped a screenshot. Birmingham-based tie company @TiedtotheSouth asks for a RT for everybody who died with a pic of Tower 1 gushing smoke pic.twitter.com/pSqoVPEXI3— Sam Thielman* (@samthielman) September 11, 2014 That same year the Twiiter account for the Timehop app, that markets itself as "a time capsule of you", posted a tweet with two photos: one showing its dinosaur mascot looking at an animated New York City cityscape with two beams of light where the towers were, and another showing the dinosaur pointing at the first photo and saying "Memba dis?" Absolutely #breathtaking 9/11 tribute: cartoon dinosaur asking "memba dis?". Do u memba? Memba when the towers fell? pic.twitter.com/pFLSwncTa6— Helena Bottom-Farter (@solikebasically) September 11, 2014 Finally, Build-a-Bear, the company that allows customers to create their own stuffed teddy bears, tweeted a now-retracted photo of a bear in fatigues, which one prominent user called tone-deaf. Hey @buildabear, do you guys have a workshop for building tone-deafness? pic.twitter.com/RY3xn662Le— Miles Kahn (@mileskahn) September 11, 2014 Some companies quietly remove the tweet, while others like AT&T, which in 2013 posted a photograph of a telephone photographing the Tribute in Light searchlights, issue an apology, tweeting: "We apologise to anyone who felt our post was in poor taste. The image was solely meant to pay respect to those affected by the 9/11 tragedy." We apologize to anyone who felt our post was in poor taste. The image was solely meant to pay respect to those affected by the 9/11 tragedy.— AT&T (@ATT) September 11, 2013 Randall Stephenson, AT&T Chairman and CEO later told AdWeek, "Yesterday, we did a post on social media intended to honour those impacted by the events of 9/11. Unfortunately, the image used in the post fell woefully short of honouring the lives lost on that tragic day." Many users have wondered why some brands feel the need to acknowledge it at all. @WhiteCastle @twerkrobot why do fast food chains keep doing this? "remember the dead. by the way, burgers"— headphone jackoff (@diss1) September 11, 2014 It becomes even more head-scratching when companies that sell adult products participate. Both Fleshlight and Intimacy Box, companies that sell adult products, tweeted about the attacks in 2014 - the latter even offered a 40 per cent discount. In fact, the practice has become common. In remembrance of 9/11 we will be doing a patriotic special drink! 15%off Vanilla Blasts if you want it dyed red... http://t.co/VRUUBqvFOB— Caffeine Supreme (@CaffeineSupreme) September 11, 2014 After the satirical website the Onion created a fake ad for Subway promising two footlong subs for $9.11 with the tagline "Fly on in for Subtember 11″ and displaying a truly offensive photograph, one location accepted the coupon as if it were real. The corporation itself quickly took issue with the satirical ad, tweeting: "Like everyone, we are deeply offended by the fake story and ad created by The Onion." Each of the incidents spark outrage. So much so that experts suggest companies avoid the sombre anniversary completely. "We've been saying to people, there's probably no right way to do this," J Walker Smith, executive chairman at the Futures Company consultancy, told the New York Times in 2011. "If I were a marketer, I would let the moment pass. Anything you do could be seen as self-serving or disrespectful." Marian Salzman, an author and marketing expert, agreed. "On one level, you want to convey a sense of empathy and sympathy and patriotism. On another level, there's a belief that every milestone in American history has been turned into a marketing opportunity," Salzman told the Times. "My advice would be to go dark. There's no place for brands to live." But if the Walmart/Coke display in Florida is any indication, some brands are still learning.  - The Washington Post Saved|Saved Stories Saved|Saved Stories Save|Saved Stories Save|Saved Stories Next World story: Facebook weeds out clickbait from News Feed, says don't rely on Facebook for all your news Business Homepage Comments business headlines Kaikoura 'needs a miracle' $5m aid package for quake farmers First tourists on the water Bike station in the heart of cycle city Kaikoura fishery closure on cards Paul Henry's wine sells out Auckland port heeds Wellington's call Mortgage fraudster jailed Gone: Jaybees jelly beans 'Ready to go' tsunami warning system on shelf South Island open for business Lifeline falls short for Seddon Roadside sheep slaughter Tables 'sparkle' at new McDonalds Queensgate still closed Ad Feedback Most popular Viewed Shared Commented Live: 7.8 New Zealand earthquake Quake action formed Hanmer Springs but latest quake passed it by Woman's acts with dog 'repulsive': judge 'Tragic death' at childcare centre on Auckland's North Shore Earthquake creates a new geographical landmark in Hurunui Car totalled after crashing into collapsed Kaikoura bridge Wellington landlords warned about building safety as confusion continues over CBD Traffic on SH7 expected to quadruple while SH1 is repaired The earthquake from an engineer's perspective Eyewitnesses describe terrifying scenes at Springvale Commonwealth Bank fire Earthquake creates a new geographical landmark in Hurunui Quake action formed Hanmer Springs but latest quake passed it by Nelson man cooks crayfish for Kaikoura earthquake refugees Finding out how much the Earth moved during massive earthquake How are we supposed to sleep? Her name was Rebekah: Aftermath of domestic violence Traci Moyer , tmoyer@newsleader.com 3:16 p.m. EDT September 12, 2016 Skip Ad Ad Loading... x Embed x Share In 2009, Rebekah Gibson, 20, a former resident of Waynesboro, was murdered by Ridge Lee Huffman in Buckhannon, W. Va. Seven years after her death, her parents, David and Nancy Jo Gibson of Waynesboro talk about their daughter and domestic violence. Holly Marcus/Special to The News Leader In the wake of a violent death, seven years later. Nancy Jo Gibson of Waynesboro had made a little scrapbook for her daughter Rebekah, who was killed at age 20 in 2009 by her boyfriend in West Virginia, that was returned to her with her daughter's belongings. (Photo: Holly Marcus / Special to The Ne) 774 CONNECTTWEETLINKEDIN 4 COMMENTEMAILMORE In the early morning hours of a cold and rainy January night in 2009, police responded to a 911 call about two people arguing in a Wal-Mart Superstore parking lot. The caller said it looked like the man was smashing up a car with a baseball bat. When the police arrived, the couple was nowhere to be found. With only a vague description of the couple and the car they drove, the police began searching for them in what is called a "rolling domestic" incident. Police did not know it at the time, but before the night was over the couple they were looking for would be involved in another incident, this one ending with the violent death of the young woman. Her name was Rebekah. * A SONG AND A PRAYER A mother and daughter, once close, are pulling apart and having difficulty communicating with each other. Despite or perhaps because of their exceptional closeness from years of homeschooling in Waynesboro, pride and protection, self-assertion and rejection get in the way. The daughter moves out. In the summer of 2008, the mother sends her a small scrapbook with a handful of childhood photos, a CD and song lyrics, trying to show her daughter what she cannot say. She prays for her child’s safe passage through young adulthood every night. The song is “In My Arms” by Plumb: “And as I watch / You start to grow up / All I can do / Is hold you tight / Knowing clouds will rage and / Storms will race in / But you will be / Safe in my arms.” The daughter thanks her mom politely for the gift, but in a journal entry she shows how truly moved she was by her mother’s gesture. “One day, mom, you’re going to know how much this means to me. It made me understand and see you in a whole new way. I love you so much. I’m sorry I have hurt you and made you so sad many times. Thank you for always seeing me even when sometimes I didn’t, and no one else did either.” By the time her mother reads this note, two years have passed. It’s a conversation she wishes they’d been able to have in person. But now that is impossible. * In the last hours before dawn of Jan. 28, 2009, Ridge Lee Huffman of Stuarts Draft parks outside his father’s house in Buckhannon, West Virginia. He walks inside  and tells his father and brother that he killed Rebekah and left her outside in the car. The family rushes out to find her body in the passenger seat, covered by a blanket. They try to reach her, but the door is locked and Huffman is inside the house, already asleep. Huffman’s brother dials 911. “I find myself asking why I couldn’t have just driven through, seen what was happening and stopped the violence before her life was taken”Lt. Doug Loudin, Buckhannon (W. Va.) Police ‘A TERRIBLE EVENT’ “It was a brutal murder,” said Matt Gregory, chief of police of Buckhannon, West Virginia. A murder the community of 5,550 living along the Buckhannon River still remembers. One man, who investigated and helped solve the crime, cannot forget it. Buckhannon Police Lt. Doug Loudin never met the victim, 20-year-old Rebekah Gibson, yet seven years after her death he vividly recalls details surrounding her murder without pulling a single police record. David and Nancy Jo Gibson of Waynesboro look through a scrapbook that Nancy Jo put together that contains memories and photos from the life of their daughter Rebekah, who was killed at age 20 in 2009 by her boyfriend in West Virginia.  (Photo: Holly Marcus / Special to The Ne) He knows she died in the early morning hours. He knows that the night before it had snowed several inches. It rained hard the night Rebekah was killed, washing away snow and blood alike from the entrance to a shopping center where Ridge Huffman pulled Rebekah from his car and smashed a Maker's Mark whiskey bottle over her head. The blow from the bottle itself was enough to kill her, according to a coroner’s report Rebekah’s father David Gibson saw. Huffman then cut her throat twice with a boxcutter and shoved her back in the car, throwing a blanket over her. In the daytime the intersection where Huffman attacked Rebekah might be among the most bustling in Buckhannon, with an Arby’s restaurant right across the access road and two gas stations and a donut shop within a few tenths of a mile. At that hour of the morning, there were no witnesses to Rebekah's murder but the rain and the mute streetlights. Loudin remembers that night because he was on patrol. He drove by the site several times within a few hours of the murder. “It always sticks in the back of my mind," he said. "Anytime I go to Wal-Mart, anytime I drive down the street where the car was found, I think about it." Several police calls were made that night by people who saw the arguing couple at different locations and different times of the night, Loudin says. Like ripples in a pond expanding outward, the information was getting to police just a little too late. After pushing Rebekah back into the car, Huffman drove around the corner to a Sheetz station.  He tried to bum a cigarette off a store clerk who was "creeped out" by him, Loudin said. Rebekah's body was outside in the parked car, visible on security video. “I find myself asking why I couldn’t have just driven through, seen what was happening and stopped the violence before her life was taken,” Loudin wrote in a letter to Rebekah’s mother Nancy Jo. “For that, I feel I failed to protect Rebekah.” Ridge Huffman drove away from the gas station, taking with him the life of a young woman. The ripple of violence widened. But it may have begun even before that night. * Rebekah, the youngest child of David and Nancy Jo Gibson of Waynesboro, was known for her love of animals, Doris Day movies and classic rock music. “She was a precious, kind, loving person who was very wounded,” said her mother Nancy Jo. “What perpetrators of domestic violence do, in my opinion, is they prey on wounded people. They manage to convince these women that this is all they are worthy of.” Buy Photo Nancy Jo and David Gibson of Waynesboro talk about their daughter, who was killed at age 20 in 2009.  (Photo: Holly Marcus/Special to The News Leader) In an effort to shield Rebekah’s mother from the details surrounding her daughter's death, the family had remained silent about Rebekah’s murder. When The News Leader retraced the lives of women who died at the hands of men in their life, the family said they wanted to share their story. Huffman, who had briefly dated Rebekah, was later sentenced to life for her murder. The story is not about him. Like a stone dropped in a pond sinks to its resting place below, he disappears from this story. It’s the ripples we are tracking. It’s the widening impact of a violent and deadly act. * PREMONITION AND GRIEF Months before her daughter’s death, Rebekah’s mother, Nancy Jo Gibson, wrote her thoughts and heartaches in a journal. All the entries start with a prayer and often beg for help. Many of the entries were filled with fears and tears. “Father, my heart is troubled over Rebekah,” Nancy Jo wrote on Dec. 6, 2008. “I do not know what, if anything is wrong, but I have a foreboding feeling.” The entries are almost psalm-like at times in asking for guidance for herself, and for Rebekah: “I ask You to be hard at work in her heart, mind, and circumstances, Father God, using all things to draw her ever closer to You and bringing her ever nearer to the place of complete surrender to You and Your will for her life.” Her concerns for her daughter’s behavior often intersect concerns that worldly attentions are pulling her away from her God. On Dec. 22, 2008, during a visit from Rebekah for the holiday, she wrote, “Father God, I confess to You that as I have been plunged back into a time of fear, grief, questioning, hurt, disappointment over Rebekah, I have pulled away from You. I am sorry, Lord. I need You desperately!” Later she realized perhaps she’d been pulling away from her daughter as well. “I didn’t stop loving them ever,” she said, speaking about her children, “but that openness of affection — I would withdraw that from them,” she said. Nancy Jo said one of her greatest regrets is refusing to visit her daughter or go to her apartment after Rebekah moved in with a boyfriend. David and Nancy Jo Gibson of Waynesboro hold a scrapbook that Nancy Jo put together that contains memories and photos from the life of their daughter Rebekah, who was killed at age 20 in 2009 by her boyfriend in West Virginia.  (Photo: Holly Marcus / Special to The Ne) Even before Rebekah came to visit for the Christmas holidays, with her new friend — Huffman, the brother of one of her roommates — who'd provided the ride from West Virginia, Nancy Jo had an uneasy feeling. “In looking back over my journaling, I felt in my heart that something was wrong before Rebekah came home on the 15th,” Nancy Jo wrote. “Those feelings of unease, however, did not prepare me for the hurt that came about when it was evident she was, once again, on a path of destruction. “What I envisioned as a wonderful Christmas with Rebekah, spent shopping, decorating, cooking, and just enjoying her was dashed when she was rarely home, being out all hours with Ridge, who had brought her home from (West Virginia). We had a few good times when she was home, but I had a very difficult time seeing her leave with this young man who was obviously a bad influence, and returning home less than the happy, respectful young woman we had last seen in (West Virginia).” The journal entries continued with Nancy Jo seeking protection for her daughter and praise for any progress between the two. They are also filled with more concern over Ridge’s presence in her daughter’s life. In January 2009, she wrote, “Rebekah left home and was staying with another girl, but was also hanging out with Ridge. Ridge’s foster father and brother came by our house looking for him. They had much concern as did we. My prayers were focused on getting Rebekah to the point where we could get her the help she desperately needed, and asking the Lord to please help me with my sadness and helplessness. “On the 28th, it was obvious something was terribly wrong.” Friends from church came over, and her husband was left work early to meet her at home. Nancy Jo was sure she knew what had happened — she was sure her prayers had been answered. “I had been praying, and was sure the Lord had answered my prayer that Rebekah be picked up by law enforcement so that she would have no option other than to allow us to get her the help she needed. “I was prepared to hear that she was in jail. It would not be fun or easy, but I felt it would open the door for her to grow strong in the Lord and become a mighty woman of God. “I was not prepared in the least to hear that my child was dead.” * Rebekah’s aunt Beth Colbert said the relationship between her niece and Huffman was similar to a phrase from a popular song — a “slow fade.” “I think it's the same with relationship violence — a jealous fit turns to being grabbed to being hit and before you know it, you are OK with being abused and defending the abuser.” Colbert said children need to be educated about the cycle of abuse and when abuse happens, people need to tell someone. She didn’t always think like this. Colbert was an adjunct instructor at Blue Ridge Community College at the time of her niece’s death. She was teaching a student orientation that had a chapter on healthy relationships and the warning signs of domestic violence and abuse. THE NEWS LEADER Special Report: Domestic Violence | newsleader.com “I skipped over it,” she said. “I thought it wasn’t that big of a deal and there were more chapters than weeks for the class. I don’t know who I thought it did happen to, but it definitely didn’t happen in my family.” After her niece’s death, Colbert extensively researched the topic of domestic violence, adding statistics — and Rebekah’s story — to the chapter’s coverage. “It’s still commonly called domestic abuse and it’s so much more than that, it’s intimate partner abuse and there are different types of abuse and relationships where it happens,” she said. “I’m not sure anyone Is talking to kids about it.” Colbert said a society tends to assign blame to the victim when domestic violence occurs. She said Rebekah found herself in a “mess,” but it’s hard to pinpoint when or how it started. “She didn't just jump from a sweet little girl to this life in West Virginia,” Colbert said. “It was a slow fade and she couldn't find her way back.” * MOTHER AND DAUGHTER Talking to Nancy Jo about her grief, some details emerge that shed direct light on Rebekah and on the softer side of their relationship. Rebekah was a perfectionist in her school work. Nancy Jo said she often put a sticker on her children’s homework telling them they did a great job, even if an answer or two was incorrect. Rebekah would peel the stickers off. Rebekah Gibson is buried in Augusta Memorial Park in Waynesboro near the edge of the cemetery where there are horses in the adjoining field, her parents, David and Nancy Jo, said she enjoyed riding horses when she was younger. Gibson, originally from Waynesboro, was killed at age 20 in 2009 by her boyfriend in West Virginia.  (Photo: Holly Marcus / Special to The Ne) “It needed to be perfect for her,” Nancy Jo said. “She did well in her studies and she would stick to her work and always get it done.” Despite how she describes herself in strict, judgmental terms, Nancy Jo was a homeschooling parent who also enjoyed a little fun with her children, with an innate understanding about some of the more enjoyable elements of public school. Nancy Jo said she home schooled her children as close to the public school system as possible — including observing snow days. “I always loved snow days when I was growing up,” she said. * There are things Nancy Jo says she could have done differently. “There was a huge layer of protection, and in my case, overprotection and insulating from reality,” she said. Nancy Jo said she kept her homeschooled children away from people who were not living the way she thought they should live, or the way God says people should live. Looking back, Nancy Jo said she is embarrassed by some of her attitudes toward people and the way she shielded her children. “Things like people with tattoos,” she said. “I would judge them and I wouldn’t want my kids around them. I don’t think that way anymore.” * Nancy Jo said there were signs her daughter was starting to pull away from the family when she was 17 — suddenly she did not want to spend time with family, and she started smoking and drinking alcohol. “She would stay out all night or we would make plans and she wouldn’t show up,” Nancy Jo said. “She became dishonest and sneaky. Deceptive. There was not that openness and there was a secrecy about things.” That’s when things started to fall apart for them both, Nancy Jo said. “I was not one to extend grace or to try to find out where the broken heart of that behavior stemmed from,” said Nancy Jo as she sat at the kitchen table and struggled to speak through her tears. “I was very unaware that pride and critical spirit and judgmental attitudes are every bit as sinful to the Lord as external behavior. “I did not recognize my need for God’s grace and therefore I was not able to extend grace.” * SCRAPBOOK Compiling a scrapbook of memories about her daughter was a constant reminder of the “hole she left in my heart,” Nancy Jo Gibson said. The scrapbook might also come as close as any of us can get to knowing what type of person Rebekah was. The Rebekah who was a daughter and sister and student and teenager; who was not a victim. David and Nancy Jo Gibson of Waynesboro hold a scrapbook that Nancy Jo put together that contains memories and photos from the life of their daughter Rebekah, who was killed at age 20 in 2009 by her boyfriend in West Virginia.  (Photo: Holly Marcus / Special to The Ne) A collection of memories in images and words reveals a girl who was the youngest of three children, the only daughter in the family. A girl who grew up in Waynesboro, who loved to ride horses and listen to an Aerosmith song or two. A vivacious, dark-haired girl whose curiosity translated well in her homeschooling, her mother said. A girl with her nose in a book. A girl who insisted on hand-raising two kittens after they were discovered in a backyard woodpile.  Or fed two baby squirrels with eyedroppers until the tiny orphans were taken to the Wildlife Center of Virginia. Sprinkled throughout the book are photos of Rebekah hugging, laughing and caught unaware by a camera lens. There is a copy of her obituary and handwritten notes from the police officer, Loudin, who investigated her death. There are also letters Rebekah wrote which were found after she was killed. While the book is crammed with scraps of paper, notes and celebrations, it fails to capture the one thing her mother misses the most — Rebekah’s laughter. Raw emotion is tucked away inside. Like the note with long space-absorbing dashes where words failed to capture a mother's feelings of loss and despair. Photos of a smiling, teenage Rebekah Jane Gibson, her hair pulled back into a smart ponytail, surround the note. * COMING HOME Lt. Loudin said Rebekah was attempting to return to her family in Waynesboro when Huffman killed her. “She missed her mom and she was going to go back and he didn’t want her to go back,” he said. “He was convinced Rebekah was his girlfriend and they were a couple,” said David Gibson, Rebekah’s father. “To be so young and murdered in such a brutal way… this forever changed our family,” her aunt Beth Colbert said. While Nancy Jo often journaled her emotions and feelings, she was unaware her daughter was doing the same. When she found her daughter’s response to the scrapbook she’d sent her in 2008, two years later and months after Rebekah’s killer had been sentenced, Nancy Jo could see she and her daughter had been closer than even she had thought. It was a singular acknowledgment of a daughter and mother’s bond, coming full circle around a ripple born of suffering, back to its source. Rebekah Gibson is buried in Augusta Memorial Park in Waynesboro near the edge of the cemetery where there are horses in the adjoining field, her parents, David and Nancy Jo, said she enjoyed riding horses when she was younger. Gibson, originally from Waynesboro, was killed at age 20 in 2009 by her boyfriend in West Virginia.  (Photo: Holly Marcus / Special to The Ne) THE NEWS LEADER Secret cousins: Black & white family 774 CONNECTTWEETLINKEDIN 4 COMMENTEMAILMORE Read or Share this story: http://www.newsleader.com/story/news/local/2016/09/08/her-name-rebekah/89660056/ TOP VIDEOS Most touching ways soldiers reunited with their family 1:17 Donald Trump's unlikely path to presidency 2:01 Worn flags retired and burned 2:18 Dad builds phenomenal costumes for his son 0:49 Fort Defiance at Waynesboro game recap 1:13 Christie's ex-aide invokes Fifth as office subpoenaed 1:06 Museum keeps school's legacy alive 1:24 Iconic 'National Geographic' 'Afghan Girl' arrested 0:41 Toxic metals found in kids' Halloween makeup 1:11 Vatican says keep your loved one's ashes off the mantel 0:24 More Stories Path to losing, keeping off pounds Nov. 16, 2016, 2:40 p.m. Alone on Thanksgiving? Even businesses that don't rely on Hanjin could be caught in cargo crisis Fortune 9/9/2016 Jeremy Quittner Click to expand Replay Video Trump rode $5 billion in free media to the White House Donald Trump didn't spend nearly as much on advertising as typical presidential candidates, and he didn't have to -- he relied on billions of dollars of free mentions in media ranging from major TV news networks to Buzzfeed and Twitter instead. The real estate magnate got $4.96 billion in free earned media in the year leading up to the presidential election, according to data from tracking firm mediaQuant. Over the past 12 months, the president-elect received more than $800 million in free earned broadcast media, compared to $666 million for Clinton, and $2.6 billion in free earned online news attention, compared to $1.6 billion for his rival. He edged out her and other major political names in American and worldwide newspapers as well. President-elect Donald Trump has called the law a "disaster." Auto Show Fox Business3:04 A look at Nashville's music industry and health care BBC News1:32 Airplane ticket prices to fall in 2017 Reuters1:11 Manufacturing in the US on a steady rise Wochit Business0:39 Canada examines possible legal cannabis system Bloomberg4:05 Will my Social Security check get bigger in 2017? Kiplinger1:12 For around $20 you can have your very own Donald Trump mask CNBC0:54 Trump signs removed from some NYC buildings CNN Money1:43 Car repairs and maintenance you can (really) do yourself GOBankingRates1:21 UP NEXT Michael Brey has a lot on his mind. Like many retail owners , the president and founder of Hobby Works, a four-location hobby and toy store based in Laurel, Maryland, is gearing up for the holiday selling season. That includes putting in orders of his specialty totes for the paraphernalia of hobby enthusiasts, which he manufactures using a Chinese factory. But he's worried his shipments will be delayed, thanks to the bankruptcy of South Korean shipping giant Hanjin, which at the end of August sent shock waves throughout the commercial world when it announced it would enter receivership. Quotes in the article Wal-Mart Stores Inc WMT ▼ 68.77 -0.42 -0.61% MSC Co Ltd 009780 ▲ 14,050.00 +450.00 +3.31% Kohl's Corp KSS ▲ 55.36 +0.85 +1.56% National Retail Properties Inc NNN ▲ 41.54 +0.08 +0.19% Not only is Hanjin responsible for nearly 8% of all trans-Pacific trade volume, but its failure comes at a time when retailers large and small are putting in their final orders with manufacturers and stocking up in preparation for the holiday shopping season. Hanjin, the seventh-largest shipper in the world, has reportedly left stranded nearly half of its fleet of 100 vessels in ports around the world. Although Hanjin is said to be working on the solution, its ships, carrying billions of dollars worth of merchandise, are unable to pay the terminal operators the various offloading and fuel surcharge fees required to get the cargo moving. Eliminating such a large carrier also constricts the shipping pipeline for new shipments until the crisis is resolved. Brey, whose company has 50 employees and annual revenue of $6 million, says he probably ships about 12 containers a year using the Evergreen Line and MSC Cargo. Yet even though he doesn't use Hanjin, he believes the shipments of his product are in jeopardy. "This is the time when all the big boys–the Walmarts and Amazons and Kohl's of the world–are pushing their factories to get their products manufactured and shipped to the states and ready to move to stores," Brey says. "If we have prearranged with [our shippers] to do two containers at the end of November, and then Walmart says we need this entire ship, guess what will happen to me."© Provided by Fortune Operations At A Hanjin Newport Co. (HJNC) Terminal The largest retailers and their vendors have well-established shipping contingency plans for emergencies such as bankruptcy or natural disasters, which enable them to shift from one carrier to another to ensure proper delivery of products, says Jonathan Gold, vice president for supply chain and customs policy for the National Retail Federation. That's not necessarily the case for smaller retailers, who lack the scale of their larger competitors. "There is the potential that smaller retailers could be harmed," Gold said. One reason is that contingency plans for smaller businesses can be radically more expensive. Freight forwarding companies such as Unitrans Worldwide, a 12-employee company based in Randolph, Massachusetts, for example, provide full-service shipping arrangements to small manufacturers and retailers. During the West Coast port shutdown in 2015, Lindsay Barich, the company's chief executive and founder, said he was able to manage deliveries to other ports throughout the U.S. Given the timing of Hanjin's bankruptcy, some of Barich's customers have found their only option is shipping their cargo by plane, he says. For example, Barich says he helped a local manufacturer and retailer of sporting goods products transport its polo shirts, golf shoes, and belts using an air carrier, so it would have the products in time for the holidays. Yet the expedited service came at a steep cost, of about $11,000 for the order, more than three times the cost of shipping the cargo by boat. "They paid an exorbitant amount of money for something that could have gone by ocean," Barich says. Related: Why Fintech Startups Are Flocking to a 124-Year-Old Bank in Kansas Rising shipping costs and delays related to the Hanjin bankruptcy are also something that Bryan Pate, the chief executive and co-founder of ElliptiGo, a San Diego-based elliptical bicycle manufacturer with 22 employees, says are now on his radar . The company ships about 40 containers worth of product a year from Taiwan, destined for 250 retailers around the U.S. as well as for sale online at its own website. Pate says his director of operations has gotten shipping estimates that are between 15% and 75% higher from his own freight forwarder, which uses Hanjin, among other large worldwide shippers. "We were shocked to hear the news," Pate says. He adds that the company could handle a small rate increase , but would have a hard time continuing to expand if rates were to jump 75%. "That would cost us about $80,000 a year, which is like adding another employee," Pate says. Obama arrives to meet European leaders after Trump's shock election win which dismayed them all The last supper: Barack Obama and Angela Merkel say farewell over an intimate meal on his final official tour of Europe Previous Next At least 23 people killed in explosion and fire at Bangladeshi packaging factory that supplies firms including Nestle and British American Tobacco  Dozens more have been injured the massive blast near Dhaka which happened earlier this morning  The fire spread very quickly because a large amount of flammable chemicals were stored at the factory 50 people could be injured - at least six burns victims at local hospital were in a critical condition It took firefighters nearly five hours to bring the blaze under control after a boiler reportedly exploded Factory safety is a major concern in Bangladesh following 2013 incident in which 1,135 people died By Paddy Dinham For Mailonline Published: 08:27 EST, 10 September 2016 | Updated: 12:46 EST, 10 September 2016 e-mail 512 shares 5 View comments A boiler exploded and triggered a fire at a packaging factory near Bangladesh's capital, killing at least 23 workers and injuring dozens, officials said. Fire officials said that the explosion at the five-story Tampaco Foils factory in the Tongi industrial area outside Dhaka was huge, and that the fire spread quickly because flammable chemicals were stored at the factory. At least six of the 14 people being treated for burns at Dhaka Medical College and Hospital were in critical condition, said Mohammed Bacchu Mia, a police official at the hospital. He confirmed that at least 23 people had died. Scroll down for video. Factory safety is a major concern in Bangladesh, which has thousands of garment and packaging factories that supply products to global chains like Wal-Mart and H&M.  In 2012, a fire at a garment factory in a Dhaka suburb killed 112 workers.  A year later, a commercial complex near Dhaka housing five garment factories collapsed, killing 1,135 people, Bangladesh's worst industrial disaster. Firefighters on a ladder spray water to put out the fire. Huge piles of burned materials and chemicals had to be removed from the building to prevent the fire from spreading further An injured person rescued from a fire is taken into an ambulance. At least six of the 14 people being treated for burns at Dhaka Medical College and Hospital were in critical condition Firefighters and local people work together to put out the fire. It took nearly five hours to bring the massive blaze under control Firefighters spray water to put out the fire. It was not immediately clear what caused the explosion, which occurred at around 6 a.m. Authorities have ordered an investigation into how exactly the fire started. major factory accidents in 2012 and 2013 prompted Bangladesh's government, global brands and the United Nations to work together to try to improve safety standards in the South Asian country's factories  It took firefighters nearly five hours to bring Saturday's blaze under control. Huge piles of burned materials and chemicals had to be removed from the building to prevent the fire from spreading further, officials said. Authorities have since ordered an investigation as to how exactly the fire broke out, but it is believed to have started when a boiler exploded. Syed Mokbul Hossain, the owner of the Tampaco Foils factory, told the Bengali-language Prothom Alo daily that he was not sure when it was last inspected. It was the last working day at the factory before the workers were to go on leave for a weeklong holiday for the Islamic festival of Eid al-Adha   A body of a fire victim is carried in to a makeshift morgue after the horrific fire in which 23 people have so far died The bodies are lined up, as officials and desperate civilians try to identify anyone from the remains Another body is carried by emergency services towards the makeshift morgue following the horrific fire that has so far claimed 23 lives Two women embrace as they watch the terror unflold, but it is a scene that Bangladeshis know only two well following recent fires He said around 75 people had been scheduled to work the overnight shift.  Saturday was the last working day at the factory before the workers were to go on leave for a weeklong holiday for the Islamic festival of Eid al-Adha, which falls on Tuesday. The major factory accidents in 2012 and 2013 prompted Bangladesh's government, global brands and the United Nations to work together to try to improve safety standards in the South Asian country's factories. You are here: Home » Companies » News Walmart to stop selling sheets made by Welspun Affected products represent around 6% of Welspun's total business Walmart will stop selling Welspun's Egyptian-cotton sheets over concerns about the products' provenance, dealing a fresh blow to a supplier embroiled in controversy. Walmart took the step after a review of Welspun's cotton sheets, a move spurred by rival Target Corporation cutting ties with the Indian vendor. Unlike Target, Walmart said it won't end all business with Welspun, which is putting stronger quality controls in place and adopting new labelling practices. "Our customers trust us to provide products that are what they say they are on the label," Marilee McInnis, a spokeswoman for Bentonville, Arkansas-based Walmart, said in an email on Friday. "Welspun has not been able to assure us the products are 100 per cent Egyptian cotton, which is unacceptable. While the sheets are excellent quality, we are offering our customers a full refund." Walmart's move threatens to further tarnish Welspun's image, though the Indian company will at least maintain a relationship with the world's largest retailer. Target said last month that it would end all business with Welspun, one of the world's biggest textile manufacturers, because the vendor was sending it phony Egyptian-cotton sheets. Since Target's decision was announced, Welspun shares have fallen 45 per cent. And other retailers have said they will probe the authenticity of their Welspun products. "We take the current traceability concerns around some of our product lines very seriously and have been working closely with our retail partners to support their actions toward a comprehensive resolution program," a Welspun spokesman said in an emailed statement on Saturday. "The affected products represent around 6 per cent of Welspun's total business." The controversy has raised awareness about cotton certification, and whether household products are indeed manufactured in their labelled country of origin. Customers often pay a premium for Egyptian-cotton products because they are perceived to be softer and more durable. Sheets made from cotton grown in other countries don't always carry the same cachet among Americans. Walmart announced on August 23 that it was reviewing Welspun's cotton certification records, as well as checking other suppliers of Egyptian-cotton products. Walmart is one of Welspun's largest customers, along with Target and Bed Bath & Beyond, which also is reviewing its Welspun products. Welspun is part of a roughly $3 billion conglomerate headed by Balkrishan Goenka - with interests spanning textiles, steel, pipes, energy and infrastructure. The company says it makes every fifth towel sold in the US and counts JC Penney Co and Macy's among its customers. Walmart sold the Welspun sheets and pillow cases under the names Better Homes & Gardens and Canopy. "If a customer believes they have these sheets, they can bring in the sheets, tags of the sheets or receipt into one of our US stores and receive a refund," McInnis said. WELSPUN IN A SPIN "Welspun has not been able to assure us the products are 100 per cent Egyptian cotton, which is unacceptable," says Walmart   Welspun, in a BSE filing, said: "Welspun is working to implement stronger control and better label the products"   A fortnight ago, US retail giant Target Corporation terminated contract with Welspun. After this, Welspun appointed EY to look into the alleged lapses   US-based retail chains Bed Bath & Beyond and JCPenney are also conducting third party audit of items sourced from Welspun Bloomberg Business Standard http://bsmedia.business-standard.com/_media/bs/wap/images/bs_logo_amp.png 177 22 India's richest techies take a hit as valuations deflate Prices will soar by up to Rs 1,000 with BS-IV norms in 2017: HMSI Business Standard Walmart to stop selling sheets made by Welspun Affected products represent around 6% of Welspun's total business Bloomberg  September 10, 2016 Last Updated at 23:30 IST email this article Message: Recipients' Email: Type address separated by commas Your Email: Enter the characters shown in the image. Welspun faces Walmart review after Target pulls sheets Welspun scandal follows years of falling Egyptian cotton output Walmart will stop selling Welspun's Egyptian-cotton sheets over concerns about the products' provenance, dealing a fresh blow to a supplier embroiled in controversy. Fire officials said that the explosion at the five-story Tampaco Foils factory in the Tongi industrial area outside Dhaka was huge, and that the fire spread quickly because flammable chemicals were stored at the factory. At least six of the 14 people being treated for burns at Dhaka Medical College and Hospital were in critical condition, said Mohammed Bacchu Mia, a police official at the hospital. He confirmed that at least 23 people had died. Scroll down for video. Factory safety is a major concern in Bangladesh, which has thousands of garment and packaging factories that supply products to global chains like Wal-Mart and H&M.  In 2012, a fire at a garment factory in a Dhaka suburb killed 112 workers.  A year later, a commercial complex near Dhaka housing five garment factories collapsed, killing 1,135 people, Bangladesh's worst industrial disaster. Post Your Comments Share Cancel Moneycontrol Bureau Welspun India will continue to do business with Walmart and is working to implement stronger controls and better label the products being supplied, the company said in a statement on Saturday. The statement came after Wal-Mart Stores Inc Friday said it will stop selling Egyptian cotton sheets made by Welspun as it was not assured about the authenticity of the products. Walmart plans to withdraw the products from its online and offline stores and provide full refund to customers. "The affected products represent around 6 percent of Welspun’s annual business. The product line in question with Walmart accounts for approximately 1.5 percent of Welspun’s annual business," the release said. Welspun has been in the midst of controversy after one of its US-based customers Target Corp last month severed all ties claiming that Welspun, for nearly two years, had been supplying sheets made of cheaper variety of cotton instead of the premium Egyptian cotton as per the deal.   The company has engaged a Big Four consultancy firm to review its processes to put to rest the "traceability concerns" with respect to its Egyptian cotton products, the statement said.   Tags  Welspun India Wal-mart Stores Inc Egyptian cotton Related Stories Welspun India shares extend fall, dip over 4% on Q2 net loss Welspun India yesterday reported a consolidated ne Will continue to have double-digit growth next year: Welspun In an interview to CNBC-TV18 Altaf Jiwani, CFO at Welspun Q2 net loss at Rs 147.52 cr on Egyptian Cotton issue Its income from operations in the quarter under re Welspun to closely monitor its Egyptian cotton business The steps to be initiated include deployment of a Welspun India: Outcome of board meeting Welspun India Ltd has informed BSE that the Board Set email alert for Welspun India : Set Alert Buy, Hold, Sell ? Ashish Pandey  | Posted by Ankit Misra  Follow @AASHISH_NEWS   pandey.ashish@aajtak.com Vijayawada, September 10, 2016 | UPDATED 16:11 IST A +A - Fire broke out at Walmart's Best Price store premises in Vijayawada early today. ANI Photo. Highlights 1 Mishap led to traffic jam on NH-16 connecting Eluru to Vijayawada. 2 No lives lost in the accident, damage to property being assessed. 3 The cause of the fire is yet to be ascertained. Property worth crores of rupees was gutted as a fire broke out at Walmart's Best Price store premises in Vijayawada in the wee hours on Saturday. The fire has been brought under control. In a statement the global retail giant said, "We are assessing the damage to the property and investigating the matter. Fortunately, no lives have been lost in this unfortunate incident and all our staff are safe." BCP TEAM TO REPAIR DAMAGED STORE "We have a robust 'Business Continuity Plan' (BCP) to handle all such issues and our BCP team has taken over to quickly repair our store. We are committed to ensuring that our esteemed customers face no disruption in services, the company said in a statement. Our customers will continue to be served through our nearby Guntur Best Price store and our online Best Price website www.bestprice.in, the statement added. Meanwhile, the cause of fire was not known immediately and is yet to be ascertained. News Sports Living Obits Item Banner Cars Jobs E-Edition Subscriber Services log in Site Archive Groups spending millions on charter school ballot question Friday Sep 9, 2016 at 6:38 PM Sep 10, 2016 at 9:10 AM Scott O'Connell Telegram & Gazette Staff @ScottOConnellTG A former New York City mayor, New England Patriots owner Robert Kraft’s company group, and two Walmart heirs are among the major donors to a ballot campaign seeking to open the door for more charter schools in the state, while teachers unions are funding the opposition effort, according to campaign finance reports. According to the state’s Office of Campaign & Political Finance, there has been a flurry of donations – much of it coming from out of state – and spending since the start of the year on Question 2 on the state’s general election ballot this fall. Supporters of the ballot question seek to authorize the state to allow up to a dozen new charter schools to open each year. They argue the autonomous public schools provide a needed alternative to regular public schools, especially in struggling urban school districts. Opponents say more charter schools, the superiority of which to regular schools they argue is still unproven, will sap even more public education money away from those underfunded public schools. According to the OCPF’s online database, there are four committees backing Question 2 this year: Great Schools Massachusetts, Expanding Educational Opportunities, Yes on Two, and the Campaign for Fair Access to Quality Public Schools. Of those, Great Schools has by far been the busiest fundraiser and biggest spender, taking in almost $8.2 million since the start of the year and spending $5.2 million. Most of those contributions came from a single source: New York-based Families For Excellent Schools Advocacy, Inc., which gave multiple donations totaling more than $5.7 million, the committee’s latest report with the OCPF shows. The committee also received a $240,000 donation from billionaire businessman and former New York City Mayor Michael Bloomberg. Several in-state donors pitched in as well, led by Lynnfield-based Strong Economy For Growth, Inc., which gave multiple contributions totaling $650,000. Great Schools spent most of its money, meanwhile, on advertising, including a combined $4.3 million on media buys. The Campaign for Fair Access committee, the next biggest fundraiser, has only recently started receiving donations since organizing in July, but has pulled in a sizeable amount of money in that short time. Of the nearly $2.3 million the committee has gotten in contributions over that period, the biggest donation came from Arvest Bank Group president Jim Walton, son of Walmart founder Sam Walton, who gave more than $1.1 million to the campaign. The committee so far has spent more than $500,000 of that haul, mostly on campaign management services. The committee dropped $450,000 alone on hiring Wellesley-based Five Corner Strategies, according to OCPF’s records. Yes on Two is also a relative newcomer to the campaign, bringing in a quick $710,100 since organizing in July. Almost all of that money came from a single donor, Mr. Walton’s sister, philanthropist Alice Walton, and all of it has already been spent, primarily as a nearly $704,000 donation to the Campaign for Fair Access committee. Lastly, Expanding Educational Opportunities brought in its entire $325,000 haul in the past month alone, $250,000 of which was then sent over to Great Schools. The committee’s only donors were the Kraft Group and Partners Healthcare, which gave $100,000 apiece, EMC Corporation, which gave $75,000, and Vertex Pharmaceuticals Incorporated, which gave $50,000. The lone committee opposing Question 2, Save Our Public Schools, has so far been outspent by the pro-question groups, but has still taken in almost $6.8 million since forming in March. It’s also spent $3.6 million over the same period on various campaign expenses, including more than $400,000 on TV advertising. The committee’s biggest donations came from teachers unions; the Massachusetts Teachers Association, for instance, gave nearly $4.2 million in multiple contributions, while the American Federation of Teachers donated just over $700,000. The National Education Association pitched in $1.9 million as well. Finance reports submitted to the OCPF on Friday satisfied the agency's requirement that all ballot campaign committees file their latest financial records 60 days in advance of the general election, which this year falls on Nov. 8. Scott O’Connell can be reached at Scott.O’Connell@telegram.com. The fire engulfed a large part of the Best Price modern wholesale store located at Nidamanur, resulting in huge loss of property. There were no casualties in the fire, suspected to have been caused by a short circuit, officials said. "A fire broke at our Best Price store premises in Vijaywada earlier today (Saturday). State Fire authorities quickly reached the store and have brought it under control. We are assessing the damage to the property and investigating the matter. Fortunately, no lives were lost in this unfortunate incident and all our employees and staff are safe," said a spokesperson of Walmart. This is one of the 21 Best Modern wholesale stores owned and operated by Walmart India across the country. Each store offers about 5,000 items in a cash and carry wholesale format. "We have a robust 'Business Continuity Plan' (BCP) to handle all such issues and our BCP team has taken over to quickly restore our store. Wal-Mart took the step after a review of Welspun's cotton sheets, a move spurred by rival Target cutting ties with the Indian vendor. Unlike Target, Wal-Mart said it won't end all business with Welspun, which is putting stronger quality controls in place and adopting new labeling practices. "Our customers trust us to provide products that are what they say they are on the label," Marilee McInnis, a spokeswoman for Bentonville, Arkansas-based Wal-Mart, said in an email on Friday. "Welspun has not been able to assure us the products are 100 percent Egyptian cotton, which is unacceptable. While the sheets are excellent quality, we are offering our customers a full refund." VIDEOS TOP JOBS Wal-Mart's move threatens to further tarnish Welspun's image, though the Indian company will at least maintain a relationship with the world's largest retailer. Target said last month that it would end all business with Welspun, one of the world's biggest textile manufacturers, because the vendor was sending it phony Egyptian-cotton sheets. Since Target's decision was announced, Welspun shares have fallen 45 percent. And other retailers have said they will probe the authenticity of their Welspun products. The controversy has raised awareness about cotton certification, and whether household products are indeed manufactured in their labeled country of origin. Customers often pay a premium for Egyptian-cotton products because they are perceived to be softer and more durable. Sheets made from cotton grown in other countries don't always carry the same cachet among Americans. Wal-Mart announced on Aug. 23 that it was reviewing Welspun's cotton certification records, as well as checking other suppliers of Egyptian-cotton products. Wal-Mart is one of Welspun's largest customers, along with Target and Bed Bath & Beyond Inc., which also is reviewing its Welspun products. Welspun is part of a roughly $3 billion conglomerate headed by Balkrishan Goenka — with interests spanning textiles, steel, pipes, energy and infrastructure. The company says it makes every fifth towel sold in the U.S. and counts J.C. Penney Co. and Macy's Inc among its customers. Wal-Mart sold the Welspun sheets and pillow cases under the names Better Homes & Gardens and Canopy. "If a customer believes they have these sheets, they can bring in the sheets, tags off the sheets or receipt into one of our U.S. stores and receive a refund," McInnis said.   Share This Article JOIN THE DISCUSSION     Post a Comment POPULAR STORIES It's not easy being black at BYU, film shows Garrison Keillor: Politics is not everything. But it’s also important how we remember. In a well-intended display at a Panama City, Fla., Wal-Mart this week, a Coca-Cola supplier brought down the righteous ire of social media by stacking cases of Coke in the shape of the Twin Towers – with red, white and blue cases behind them in the shape of an American flag. The display was taken down and an apology offered. We have no doubt both the display and apology were sincere. But it’s a cautionary tale for retailers across the country: Mixing solemn remembrances with retail sales is a delicate matter indeed, and probably ought to be avoided all together. “Delicate” is hardly the word to describe a TV commercial a San Antonio mattress retailer ran recently, which featured a 9/11-themed “Twin Tower Sale.” Unbelievably, the ad sported two “towers” of mattresses that are – supposedly comically – knocked down at the end of the spot. “What better way to remember 9/11 than with a Twin Tower sale?” a woman asks in the commercial. After the shameless plug and presumed hilarity, the woman incongruously seizes up in a moment of seriousness to say “We’ll never forget.” We’d rather she did – if this is how she’s going to remember. It’s the most disgusting advertisement, and the most garish display of raw, ugly, exploitative consumerism that you will ever see. What were these people thinking? It certainly wasn’t about the 3,000 dead on 9/11, or their many thousands of survivors, or the many millions of Americans who still mourn that horrific event to this day. What creates such empty-headed emotional detachment from such a historic atrocity? Surely it’s not just time: It’s only been 15 years – and we’ve certainly done a much better job of respectfully commemorating the attack on Pearl Harbor, which was back in 1941. Maybe present-day Americans – better fed and enjoying more creature comforts than any people in history, and removed from the mandatory military service that might open our eyes wider – have lost a sense of reverence that used to ground us. Just look at our entertainment media, in which absolutely nothing is sacred and everything is fair game for mockery. Take the raunchy adult cartoon Family Guy, which is even billed – admiringly – as “sick” and “twisted.” The show once included a joke that rescued kidnapping victim Elizabeth Smart had brought music back to her family’s home – but that most of the songs were about rape. Do these people not realize there are human beings on the other end of these vulgar outbursts? We need to remember 9/11 solemnly – not with mattress sales as if it’s nothing more than George Washington’s birthday. But more important, we could honor the victims of 9/11 by forming a more perfect union – with citizens who are educated and reverential to the past – to our forebears and their tribulations, to the fact that we stand on their shoulders today, and to our contemporaries who still suffer the gashing wounds of 9/11, war and terrorism. Of course, to grasp the first thing about inhumanity, much less the depth of its touch, one must first explore one’s humanity. It appears we’ve got some work to do on that. Welspun faces Walmart review after Target pulls sheets Welspun scandal follows years of falling Egyptian cotton output New review knot for Welspun, investors Welspun continues losing run; Rs 4,867-cr investor wealth lost Walmart Stores Inc on Friday said it will stop selling Egyptian cotton sheets made by Welspun India after the Indian manufacturer was unable to assure them the products were authentic. Last month, US retailer Target Corp severed ties with Welspun after accusing them of passing off cheap sheets as premium Egyptian cotton for two years. "Welspun has not been able to assure us the products are 100% Egyptian cotton, which is unacceptable," Walmart said in a statement. The company will pull the products from its stores and website. Walmart said it will not cut ties with Welspun but will work with them to implement strong controls and better label the products. The retailer will offer customers, who purchased the products, a full refund. Egyptian cotton is prized because the length of the cotton fibers are longer, resulting in a finer, lighter more durable fabric and longer-lasting, higher-end clothing. STEPHEN, NEW BRUNSWICK — A man from Maine was arrested Wednesday after he used an air mattress purchased from Walmart to paddle across the St. Croix River and into Canadian territory, according to the Portland Press Herald. John Michael Bennett, 25, of Calais, Maine, claimed he was very concerned about his pregnant fiancee, who, he said, was in danger because of a violent ex-boyfriend. After attempting and failing to enter the country through an official border station, Bennett went to the local Walmart and bought both an air mattress and a paddle that he subsequently used to cross the river into Canada. Authorities say Bennett was rejected from the border station due to a pending criminal mischief charge he has in Calais. Bennett took the air mattress to a riverbank and inflated it, before getting in it and paddling across the "1,000 to 2,000 feet wide" section of river. Bennett's crossing was reported to authorities by a Canadian resident, after which Bennett was picked up by border patrol agents and police on Ledge Road in St. Stephen. Bennett appeared in court on Thursday and pleaded guilty to crossing into Canada illegally. As a result, he was sentenced to two months in jail and will also be deported to the U.S. after his sentence is over. "Although this was somewhat comedic in terms of how he came across, the larger message needed to be sent out to the public on both sides of the border that the penalties will be significant no matter what the circumstances," said Peter Thorn, a lawyer representing the federal Public Prosecution Service of Canada.   MASSLIVE ON SOCIAL MEDIA MassLive News on Facebook MassLive News on Twitter MassLive Instagram Breaking News newsletter When the big stories break, we'll send you an alert. Username or e-mail: * Password: * Create new account Request new password Close Home » News » Local Walmart shoplifter gets probation Fri, 09/09/2016 - 12:35pm | Mary Schenk URBANA — A Piper City man who admitted stealing electronics from the Champaign Walmart over several days earlier this year — then selling them to a resale shop — has been sentenced to a year of probation. Ryan Deatley, 32, pleaded guilty before Judge Heidi Ladd on Friday to retail theft over $300, admitting that between March 22 and 29, he stole controllers for three different kinds of video game systems on three different days from the Walmart, 2610 N. Prospect Ave., C. Champaign police later learned that Deatley and another man then sold those new controllers to the Disc Replay store at 2012 N. Prospect Ave., C. Deatley was also ordered to perform 75 hours of public service. Assistant State’s Attorney Tim Sullivan said Deatley had prior convictions for aggravated criminal sexual abuse, driving under the influence, domestic battery, trespass, disorderly conduct and forgery.  Sections (2):News, Local More Local What's In A Name? Sign up for The Power Lunch: Florida Politics newsletter - our must-read, weekday roundup of Florida political news and buzz >> Local News Broward News Margate News Broward deputy accused of shoplifting at WalMart 7 times, once while in uniform, records show Broward deputy accused of shoplifting at WalMart 7 times, once while in uniform, records show Surveillance video shows Broward Sheriff's Deputy Dean Korenic, 46, shoplifting on seven occasions, investigators say. Surveillance video shows Broward Sheriff's Deputy Dean Korenic, 46, shoplifting on seven occasions, investigators say. Tonya AlanezContact ReporterSun Sentinel A Broward deputy was in uniform when he was videotaped shoplifting from WalMart, arrest documents show Privacy Policy A Broward sheriff's deputy finds himself suspended without pay and facing a felony charge after being accused of shoplifting everyday household items from two WalMarts in Coral Springs, according to records obtained Friday by the Sun Sentinel. Surveillance video shows Deputy Dean Korenic, 46, shoplifting on seven occasions, investigators say. He was in uniform one of the times and drove away with his stolen goods in a marked patrol car three other times, records show. A 14-year veteran of the agency, Korenic was arrested Tuesday and spent a night in jail before posting $3,500 bond on a felony charge of scheme to defraud/obtain property under $20,000, records show. "In review of the video ... the theft was apparent and intentional," an affidavit said. "The thefts were committed both in and out of BSO uniform." Sheriff's officials would not provide the videos to the Sun Sentinel Friday. Korenic, of Margate, was suspended without pay Tuesday. He makes $72,735. Korenic was initially suspended with pay when he was first advised of the investigation on June 6. On the deputy's alleged shopping list: Cool Water cologne, Jergens lotion, papertowels, disposable razors, detergent, syrup, toothpaste, bar soap, a canister of Maxwell House coffee and a carton of eggs. Dean Korenic Broward Sheriff's Office/Courtesy Deputy Dean Korenic. Deputy Dean Korenic. (Broward Sheriff's Office/Courtesy) "It's discouraging to see and read and hear about," Sheriff Scott Israel said. "He disgraced the badge, but at this time I choose to focus on the men and women in our public corruption unit whose job it is to investigate deputies who don't do everything the right way. They got right to it, they investigated it thoroughly. We're not going to tolerate police misconduct and deputies committing illegal acts." Despite four voicemail messages left on Korenic's home and cellphones, he could not be reached for comment. It was unclear if he had an attorney. The police union generally doesn't provide lawyers for law enforcement charged with crimes not associated with their jobs. It's discouraging to see and read and hear about. He disgraced the badge. — Broward Sheriff Scott Israel Although each alleged theft was for minor amounts — $34.13 on May 13, $49.54 on May 27 and $7.27 on June 16 — all totaled the scheme adds up to a 3rd-degree felony punishable by up to 5 years in prison. The deputy had a system, according to an affidavit in support of his arrest warrant. He would do his shopping, go to a self-checkout and scan some items but not all. Korenic would slip the unscanned items into his shopping bag and leave the store, the affidavit said. The first alleged theft was committed May 13 at a WalMart located at 6001 Coral Ridge Drive. When Korenic struck there again on May 23 he was wearing "a BSO patrolman's green short sleeve Class B uniform," the affidavit said. When Korenic returned June 3 he was dressed in "civilian attire" but drove his marked cruiser. His final shoplifting spree at that store was June 18, records show. Two of the three times Korenic stole from a WalMart at 3801 Turtle Creek Drive he left in his patrol car. He wore street clothes each time — May 27, June 5 and June 16, the affidavit said. Store security picked up on Korenic on June 3 when he was seen concealing a bottle of cologne in a pair of grey slippers. A loss-prevention officer followed him to the parking lot and saw him get into a patrol car. The officer took down the plate and car numbers, records show. A loss-prevention manager next performed an audit of the debit card Korenic used and came up with numerous transactions which helped investigators identify Korenic's other alleged thefts. "Korenic was readily identified via video, his tattoos and by the use of his personal Chase debit card," Detective Joshua Web wrote in the affidavit. The videos could not be released Friday, a sheriff's spokeswoman said, because the detective working the case had them and would not return to the office until Monday. Investigators on June 6 picked up Korenic from an off-duty detail at the central terminal for Broward County Transit in downtown Fort Lauderdale and took him to the sheriff's internal affairs office. While Korenic was advised of the investigation and suspended with pay, detectives searched the trunk of his patrol car. There they found a pair of gray slippers in a WalMart bag. And in the driver's door pocket was 2-ounce bottle of Jergens lotion. tealanez@sunsentinel.com, 954-356-4542 or Twitter @talanez Copyright © 2016, Sun Sentinel Crime Theft Law Enforcement Broward County Sheriff's Office Shoplifting deputy Miramar officer guilty of stealing liquor from theft suspects BSO detention deputy accused in Wal-Mart shoplifting spree All Sections News Sports Broward Palm Beach Entertainment Classified Obituaries 78°

A  judge ordered John Donato, 64, jailed on a $5,000 cash bond during a court appearance Friday. According to police reports, Donato assaulted  the girls, ages 8 and 13, in the Wal-Mart store in late  August in a school supplies aisle.  Donato's preliminary hearing for prosecutors to present evidence justifying the charges is Sept. 15, court records said. Donato is charged with two felonies - second-degree sexual assault of a child and sexual contact with a child under 13. If convicted, he could face 100 years in prison and thousands of dollars in fines. News Sports Life Obituaries E-Edition Autos Jobs Real Estate Classifieds Site Archive East Main Street in Barstow to close on evenings, weekends Friday Sep 9, 2016 at 3:50 PM Sep 14, 2016 at 2:58 PM Mike Lamb @mlambdispatch BARSTOW — Work to lower Frontier Communications' optic lines in front of the Super Wal-Mart construction site will close down East Main Street on weekends and after 6 p.m. during the week, according to a city official. "On Sept. 12, this Monday, they are going to start with the Frontier line lowering," Consulting City Engineer Brad Merrell reported to the City Council Tuesday. "Basically, they will have two-way traffic on East Main during working hours with flaggers. "Under those conditions, it will take them three more weeks just to lower the fiber optic lines. And that doesn't include the water lines. We haven't touched that phase. We are only going to do one at a time. So on Monday, they are are going to start with Frontier line." Merrell said the decision by Shames Construction to conduct night and weekend work and keeping traffic flowing during business hours during the week was made after request by Dr. B.V. Reddy at July Council meeting. Reddy owns a veterinary clinic next door to the Humane Society in the 2500 block of East Main Street. Reddy said he was representing many of the businesses and residents along East Main Street affected by the construction that at times blocks traffic for hours. He asked the Council during the public comment period for the city and Wal-Mart contractor to come up with some alternative plans to keep traffic moving. "Speed up the process as much as they can," Reddy said. "Our main priority is to see if you can convince (the contractor) to use one lane only and let the traffic use the other lane at lower speed. Put in some speed bumps. Stuff like that. "They (construction workers) do not work evenings, nights, weekends, holidays. They just come in the mornings at 8 or 9 o'clock and quit at 3, 4 o'clock. Obviously at that speed it will delay the whole job." Mike Lamb can be reached at 760-957-0613 or mlamb@desertdispatch.com. You can also follow him on Twitter @mlambdispatch. 'Welspun has not been able to assure us the products are 100% Egyptian cotton, which is unacceptable. While the sheets are excellent quality, we are offering our customers a full refund,' Wal-Mart spokeswoman Marilee McInnis said. Earlier, Walmart's rival Target had also announced it would pull Egyptian cotton Welspun sheets from its shelves and offering refunds to the customers. Target also cut ended all the dealings with the Indian vendor. Christian Sanchez, 48, is now charged with a petty misdemeanor count of larceny. LCPD detectives had originally charged Sanchez with felony counts of robbery and conspiracy but the Third Judicial District Attorney’s Office dismissed those charges. Sanchez’s girlfriend, 36-year-old Shana Kowalke, was originally charged with a felony count of conspiracy to commit robbery but that charge also was dismissed by the DA’s Office. She no longer faces charges in this case. Officers were dispatched to the incident that occurred at about 8 p.m. Saturday, Sept. 3, at the Walmart store on Walton Boulevard. Detectives learned that a 19-year-old woman was leaving the store, carrying a bag of ice in each hand, with her wallet tucked underneath one arm. As she exited the store a man wearing a blue and white plaid shirt, later identified as Sanchez, approached from behind and ripped away the wallet from the woman. The victim gave chase as the suspect ran north into the parking lot. The victim yelled for help and caught up to the man, striking him several times in the head. Bystanders helped detain the man until police arrived. Detectives reviewed surveillance video from Walmart that indicates Sanchez and Kowalke were inside the store only a few seconds before Sanchez followed the victim outside. Detectives also have reason to believe that Kowalke helped Sanchez commit the crime by pointing out the victim. Magistrate Court issued a warrant for the arrest of Sanchez. Once he’s detained, he’ll be held on a $2,000 surety bond. Economy Federal Reserve Capitol Report Economic Report Columns Darrell Delamaide Irwin Kellner Rex Nutting Tools Economic Calendar Real Estate Location Scouts realtor.com My MarketWatch Watchlist Alerts Games Log In Home Industries Retail/Wholesale The Wall Street Journal Get email alerts The Wall Street Journal Wal-Mart to stop selling Welspun India’s Egyptian cotton sheets By Sarah Nassauer and Preetika Rana Published: Sept 9, 2016 5:00 p.m. ET Share Retail giant joins others in questioning advertised cotton content Getty Images Looking for Welspun sheets at Wal-Mart? Look no further. By SarahNassauer PreetikaRana Wal-Mart Stores Inc. said it would stop selling Egyptian cotton sheets made by Welspun India Ltd., after its investigation found the Indian textile giant couldn’t guarantee the products were legitimate. “Welspun has not been able to assure us the products are 100% Egyptian cotton, which is unacceptable,” Wal-Mart WMT, -0.33%  spokeswoman Marilee McInnis said. The world’s biggest retailer is removing the Welspun products from U.S. store shelves and Walmart.com. Wal-Mart said it would offer customers who purchased the products a full refund. It will donate the sheets currently on shelves. The move is the latest blow to the Indian textile company after Target Corp. TGT, +0.11%  last month said it was pulling thousands of Welspun’s “Egyptian cotton” sheets from its shelves and cutting ties with the company after it found Welspun had not used actual Egyptian cotton in the products for about two years. Target’s move spurred other Welspun customers, including Wal-Mart, J.C. Penney Co. JCP, +0.14%  and Bed Bath & Beyond Inc. BBBY, -0.16%  also to investigate the products. Penney and Bed Bath & Beyond on Friday didn’t immediately respond to requests for comment. An expanded version of this report appears at WSJ.com. Walmart Pulls Welspun Not-Egyptian Cotton Sheets From Stores, Offers Refunds Share on Facebook Share on Twitter RSS Feed Tweet Share Walmart Pulls Welspun Not-Egyptian Cotton Sheets From Stores, Offers Refunds Image courtesy of JoelZimmer September 9, 2016 3:50 pm EST By Laura Northrup@lnorthrup not egyptian welspun fieldcrest egyptian cotton cotton sheets better homes and gardens canopy walmart After Target pulled sheets that it says were mislabeled as Egyptian cotton from its shelves, dropped the supplier, and offered refunds to customers, other stores that carry products from the same supplier conducted their own reviews. Walmart announced today that it will no longer sell the company’s Egyptian cotton sheets and will give shoppers refunds, but won’t drop the company as a supplier like Target did. If you bought Fieldcrest brand Egyptian cotton sheets from Target in the last two years or so, you may be due a refund. The retailer discovered that Welspun had substituted another type of cotton while labeling the sheets as Egyptian cotton, yet the mislabeled products still sold for up to $75. Now Walmart is also issuing refunds, having sold sheets made from the same problematic fiber under its home-goods brands Better Homes & Gardens and Canopy. The retailer promises refunds to customers who bring in the affected sheets, their tags, or a receipt from purchasing the sheets for a refund. “Our customers trust us to provide products that are what they say they are on the label,” a Walmart spokeswoman told Bloomberg Markets. “Welspun has not been able to assure us the products are 100 percent Egyptian cotton, which is unacceptable. While the sheets are excellent quality, we are offering our customers a full refund.” Shoppers pay premium prices for long-fiber cotton types like Pima or Egyptian. This sheet scandal might lead those shoppers to question the entire idea of labeling: if you can’t depend on the label to tell you the origin and contents of a product, what can you depend on? That’s a scary prospect for sheet-makers and retailers alike. The importance of labels is what led Target, Walmart, and another retailer of Welspun products, Bed Bath and Beyond, to review the products and reconsider their relationship with the supplier. (For the Chronicle/Gary Fountain, September ... more Photo: Gary Fountain, Gary Fountain/For The Chronicle Image 20 of 20 Revamped Walmart store reopens in west Houston 1 / 20 Back to Gallery Walmart marked the grand reopening Friday of a west Houston store, one of hundreds the retailer plans to remodel this year. The store, at 2700 S. Kirkwood, features an expanded produce area, an expanded deli, a new pharmacy and a changed layout of its customer service and pickup areas. Those are among the same changes the retailer plans to complete at about 400 stores nationwide. Walmart officials have said the goal is to increase shopper convenience. Recently in the Houston area, similar changes were made to the Walmart store on Broadway Street in Pearland. Other retailers also are remodeling their store layouts. Recent examples include the Randalls store in Midtown Houston, Fiesta Market on South Wayside Drive and Kroger's three-year program to add and remodel existing stores in the Houston area.
